5. SCIENCE, MEDICINE

Viruses vary in size very greatly, but even the biggest, such as the influenza virus, are invisible under an ordinary microscope. The smallest, such as the poliovirus, are only a hundred times the diameter of a single carbon atom. They can be dissolved, purified and crystallised like any chemical. They behave like very large molecules and start to live only on entering the host. Apart from the chemicals contributed to the growth of the virus by the host, the virus itself contains only two substances: nucleic acid and protein. These are very complex substances. A molecule of sulphuric acid, for example, contains seven atoms; a molecule of penicillin contains forty. A molecule of sugar has forty five, but the nucleic acid molecule of one of the simplest viruses consists of 224,000 atoms and its protein molecule consists of about 2,500. Nucleic acids and proteins have quite different chemical compositions, but they have one important feature in common: they both consist of small units linked together into long chains.

Strüktürler: 1. İsim tamlaması, 2. Fiilden sonra gelen mastar, 3. ON'dan sonra gelen fiil ismi, 4. Past participle takımı.

Sözlük

to consist of

-den meydana gelmek

özellik, hususiyet

6. PSYCHOLOGY, SOCIOLOGY, BIOLOGY, MEDICINE

Do different animals behave differently because of a difference in their heredity, or because of a difference in environment? In other words, is the difference instinctive or learned? In some cases the answer is clear. Sometimes mutated genes cause a difference in behaviour and this is the result of hereditary factors influencing growth. It is quite easy to teach rats to do something new. For instance, rats can be taught to run quickly through a maze or jump towards a door labelled with a triangle. But this question of instinct or learning is seldom so easy to answer. There has been a great deal of argument about it among biologists. Both the genes and an environment are essential for the development of any pattern of behaviour. One can learn a great deal from limiting the experience of an animal during its growth, and then observing its resulting behaviour. It is difficult to do experiments to study this process of evolution in behaviour, but behaviour can be changed by artificial selection. Behaviour patterns are favoured by natural selection.

Strüktürler: 1. Past participle sıfatı, 2. Present participle + nesnesi, 3. It + to be + sıfat + mastar + nesnesi, 4. Fiilden sonra gelen mastar, 5. Past participle takımı, 6. Fiil ismi + nesnesi, 7. Present participle sıfatı, 8. Maksat gösteren mastar, 9. İsim tamlaması.

7. SCIENCE, GEOLOGY, GEOGRAPHY, ARCHAEOLOGY

Obviously the earth consists of a number of different kinds of material. Gold, for example, can exist pure in nature, and long ago it was noticed and collected as a rarity by the Egyptians. It looked quite a different kind of material from the surrounding rocks and stones.

Sayfa 135

During the gradual development of the science of chemistry, ninety two different elements have been identified as the normal components of everything on earth. An element cannot be separated into anything simpler by chemical means. During the centuries a very great deal of information has been collected about different types of materials. The Assyrians and the Egyptians probably began systematic recording. From very early times they developed the ability to recognise different ores. From these they could expect to obtain seven different metals - gold, silver, tin, copper, mercury, lead and later, iron.

Strüktürler: 1. Edat takımları, 2. Present participle sıfatı, 3. Mastar + nesnesi.

8. GEOLOGY, GEOGRAPHY

The balance of weights in the earth's crust is being continually upset. Apart from the great internal convections pushing and pulling at the surface from below, there are forces at work from above. Sea waves erode the shore, and drop the sand and pebbles offshore. Rainwater slowly washes away mountains and deposits their substance as silt in the plains below.

Sayfa 136

As a result the rock under the plains must sink under the added weight, and the rocks under the mountains rise slightly. In this way a continent can grow from its oldest region. Depressions in the earth's crust formed by downwards pulling currents deep in the earth, can fill with sediments. Then sooner or later, the subterranean currents will change, the down-pull will stop and the rather light rocks formed from the sediments will move upwards to make new mountains, with fish bones and seashells on their summits. The continents move over the surface of the earth.

Strüktürler: 1. Present participle takımı, 2. Past participle sıfatı, 3. Past participle takımı, 4. Maksat gösteren mastar.

Sayfa 137

9. SCIENCE, ASTRONOMY, HISTORY

The first scientific attempt to describe the universe was made in Greece during the first five centuries B.C. It was based on certain rules. For example, the motion of the heavenly bodies must occur in perfectly circular orbits at uniform speed. Aristotle's model succeeded in explaining the motion of the sun and planets quite well, but only by supposing them to be attached to many separate concentric spheres-each having its particular speed of rotation. But even this did not explain the variations of the distances of the planets and Ptolemy introduced epicyclic motion: that is to say, the planets moved in perfect circles about points themselves moving in perfect circular motion. From the Greeks and through the Middle Ages, man's understanding of the universe made no appreciable progress. In the thirteenth century Aristotle's teachings were revived. These were conclusions shown to disagree with the observed universe 1,100 years earlier. The solution to the problems of the motions of the planets was found by Copernicus. In 1543 his teaching showed the rotation of the earth and the planets round the sun. Kepler later introduced the idea of planet motion round the sun in elliptical orbits. Kepler's later work relating their periods of rotation to their distance from the sun was the first step towards the formulation by Newton in 1687 of his universal law of gravitation. By now the solar system was reasonably well understood. The earth was only one of a number of bodies of similar size moving under the influence of the sun's gravitational field. It could no longer claim to be unique in having the Moon, for Galileo had discovered the satellites of Jupiter.

Strüktürler: 1. Mastar + nesnesi, 2. Edattan sonra gelen present participle + nesnesi, 3. Fiilden sonra gelen mastar, 4. Present participle takımı, 5. Past participle takımı, 6. Past participle sıfatı, 7. İsim tamlaması, 8. Edilgen fiile karışan zarf.

Sözlük

şekillendirme, formüle etme

bağlı olmak

yer çekimi

10. BOTANY, FORESTRY, MEDICINE

There are two main groups of food. The body builders are needed for growth and tissue repair. For this, foods rich in nitrogen in the form of protein and other elements are required. The fuel or energy foods provide heat and energy for living. Carbohydrates and fats are the most important of these. A seed provides all these in the young plant and so it is rich in these substances. Therefore a large part of our plant food consists of seeds. The pea belongs to the family Leguminosae. Its members extract free nitrogen from the atmosphere with the help of bacteria growing in their roots. As a result, peas are rich in protein or nitrogenous food materials. Beans are also leguminous plants and their seeds possess much nutritive value. The plant grows in the form of a bush and grows best in sandy soil treated with manure. Broad beans (faba vulgaris) grow best in heavy clay soil.

Strüktürler: 1. İsim tamlaması, 2. Edattan sonra fiil ismi, 3. Edat takımları, 4. İsim + Pres. Part + edat takımı, 5. İsim + Past. Part + edat takımı.

11. ECONOMICS

By the Investment System developed in the nineteenth century, the active business class could rely not only on their own wealth but also on the savings of the whole community. The professional and propertied classes, on the other hand, could find a use for their resources, with little trouble, no responsibility and small risk. For a hundred years the system worked throughout Europe with great success, and facilitated the growth of wealth on a large scale. To save and to invest became the duty and the delight of a large class. The savings were seldom withdrawn and, accumulating at compound interest, made possible great material developments in business and industry.

Strüktürler: 1. İsim tamlaması, 2. Past participle takımı, 3. Mastar, 4. Edilgen fiile karışan zarf, 5. Present participle takımı.

12. FORESTRY

Wood was probably the first vegetable product used by man for anything other than food. Today large quantities of wood are used for a great variety of purposes. The two most important are building and paper-making. Timber is divided into two classes softwoods and hardwoods. Softwoods include the coniferous trees, such as pine and fir. Softwoods are used for most building purposes and they are easy to work. Hardwoods are the timber of certain deciduous trees, such as oak, ash and beech. Many tropical trees, like teak, provide hardwoods. The cork oak is an evergreen tree native to western Mediterranean countries. The cork used commercially is the thick, soft bark of the tree. It can be peeled off the trunk and larger branches. It grows again and can be harvested every eight to ten years.

Strüktürler: 1. İsim tamlaması, 2. İsim + past part. + edat takımı, 3. Past participle takımı.

13. ECONOMICS

The British cotton industry is suffering from competition from other parts of the world: Japan provides cheap labour and the U.S.A. has mechanised production methods. To widen the industry's market, many technical advances for cotton goods have been made. Coal became the basis of industries developed during the Industrial Revolution, and the 14 million tons produced annually in Lancashire are mostly used in local industry. The rich deposits of iron ore in the same areas assisted the development of the iron and steel industry. This has played a very important part in the economic development of the whole country.

14. GEOGRAPHY, GEOLOGY

The geologists studying the earth's crust and its large-scale movements have made an important discovery in recent years. There are two great lines of movement of the earth's crust meeting to form the letter T. Nearly all the volcanoes are found within this great T, and all the vast mountain ranges, and all the worst earthquakes. Indonesia lies completely within this T and its form is still being changed. By the eruption of the Krakatoa volcano in 1886, the little island was destroyed. Nearly all the smaller islands of this area are of volcanic or coral origin. Of the 458 active volcanoes on earth, more than half are situated in Indonesia.

Strüktürler: 1. Present participle takımı, 2. İsim tamlaması, 3. Edat takımları, 4. Edilgen fiile karışan zarf.

15. SCIENCE, ASTRONOMY, HISTORY

In his great work, Copernicus described his ideas of the structure of the universe. The sun was centre and the earth was not stationary, but travelled round the sun once a year. The earth also turned round on its own axis, and this rotation caused the change of night and day. He also described the movement of five other known planets in their orbits around the sun. He also described the moon's rotation around the earth.

Sayfa 143

Some of his theories have since been proved wrong. For example, the sun is not the centre of the universe; it is merely one of millions of other stars in the Milky Way. But his work had a great influence on other astronomers, such as Galileo, and it was the foundation of astronomical knowledge since the fifteenth century.

Strüktürler: 1. Edat takımları, 2. Edilgen fiile karışan zarf.

16. BIOLOGY

Reptiles differ from amphibians in having a skin covered with scales. They may also possess bony shields embedded in their skins. The skin of the reptile is not moist but dry. The nostrils are situated on each side of the muzzle and their sense of smell is well-developed. Snakes can also be said to use their tongues for 'smelling'. With them, they collect scent molecules from the air and carry them to a sense organ in the mouth. The external ear of most reptiles is an opening in the head, but this is not present in the snake, so it is deaf to ordinary sound.

Sayfa 144

Most reptiles reproduce by laying eggs. Their brains are similar to those of fish and amphibians, but the fore-brain is larger. They breathe by means of lungs, but these are less well-developed than the lungs of birds or mammals. The body-temperature of reptiles is not kept at constant level, but may become hot during the day, and cooler at night.

Strüktürler: 1. IN + ...ing + nesne, 2. Past part. + edat takımı, 3. Fiile karışan zarf, 4. Edat takımları, 5. Mastar nesnesi, 6. Edat + fiil ismi, 7. İsim tamlaması, 8. BY + ...ing + nesne.

17. MEDICINE, HISTORY

There are very few cases of smallpox in Britain today, but 150 years ago it was common and greatly feared. At the beginning of the 18th century more than half a million people died of smallpox every year in Europe. Besides marking the body, smallpox often causes blindness or deafness. Inoculation against the disease was first introduced into England at the beginning of the 18th century by Lady Mary Montagu, the wife of the English Ambassador in Turkey. She had observed Turkish doctors inoculating their patients successfully and she returned to England with descriptions of the new treatment. However, not all inoculations were successful and some were fatal. For every 300 people inoculated, 4 died.

Sayfa 145

But later the methods and the serum were improved and in the 19th century, vaccination against smallpox was made compulsory in many countries. It is now no longer compulsory in Britain, and the disease has almost disappeared there.

Strüktürler: 1. Edat takımları, 2. Edat + fiil ismi, 3. Edilgen fiile karışan zarf, 4. Present part. + nesnesi, 5. Past part. sıfatı, 6. Fiile karışan zarf.

18. HISTORY, LITERATURE

The year 1492 is often used to mark the end of the Middle Ages and the beginning of modern history. Christopher Columbus had landed in America in this year and this event changed the whole course of history. At this time, Spain was divided into a number of kingdoms - the most important was Aragon, but in 1476 Ferdinand of Aragon and Isabella of Castile were married, and in this way the two largest provinces were united. Spaniards played an important part in the wave of discovery of the 16th century, and much of South and Central America came under Spanish control. France had just finished a long period of civil war and the Hundred Years' War with England had just ended. Louis XI and Charles VIII brought new order to France and she was ready to expand.

Sayfa 146

In England also, civil war had ended at about this time and the country had been in a state of great disorder. Henry VII had come to the throne in 1485 and he brought peace and a strong government. Commercial development soon followed.

19. ASTRONOMY

The main body of the sun is opaque and has a visible surface known as the photosphere. This is the source of almost all the light and heat radiated by the sun. Outside the photosphere for a distance of about 6,000 miles is the chromosphere. This is a layer of transparent gases in continual movement. Above the chromosphere and covering an area many times larger than the diameter of the sun is another zone of transparent gases called the corona. Both the corona and chromosphere are normally invisible. They can be seen however during a total solar eclipse. Then the body of the moon exactly covers the photosphere and shuts out the bright light radiated from it. The sun is the centre of the solar system and it is the only important source of light and heat for the earth. Consequently it controls all forms of life. It is however, a comparatively unimportant star situated in the Milky Way at about 25,000 light years away from the centre of the galaxy. The sun consists of a globe of gas heated by thermonuclear reactions in its interior.

Strüktürler: 1. Past part. takımı, 2. Edat takımları, 3. Present part. takımı.

20. SCIENCE

The atoms of a molecule are held together by electrical forces: On dissolving in water, the molecules of certain substances split into electrically charged atoms, or groups of atoms, known as ions. For example, sodium chloride in water produces positively charged sodium ions and negatively charged chloride ions. Such substances are known as electrolytes, and solutions of them in water will conduct electricity. On passing between two conductors immersed in such a solution, an electric current causes the ions around the conductors to lose their charge and to become neutral atoms, and they can no longer remain in solution. This process is known as electrolysis. Water is partly split into ions, and the passage of an electric current will cause the water ions to lose their charges and become neutral. They are released as hydrogen and oxygen gases. Electrolysis is an important process in the chemical industry today.

Strüktürler: 1. ON + ing, 2. Past part. sıfatı, 3. Past part. takımı, 4. İsim tamlaması, 5. Mastar + nesnesi, 6. Edilgen fiile karışan zarf.

salmak, serbest bırakmak

force

yarılmak, ayrışmak

21. GEOGRAPHY, GEOLOGY, FORESTRY

Most valleys were formed by rivers. Streams flowing down the side of a hill collect at the lowest point and cut a narrow channel. Other

Sayfa 149

waters join the stream and the slope gradually becomes less steep. The river flows more slowly and the riverbed will become shallower and wider. The river now carries with it earth and stones gathered on the way down and these help to cut away the banks. Another type of valley was formed by glaciers. The ice grinds deeply into the ground and smooths out any ridges in its path. As a result, glacier valleys usually have deep flat bottoms and steep sides and they are much straighter than river valleys. The glacier collects the rocks in its path, breaks them up and deposits them over the ground. Glacier valleys can be recognised by scratches or ridges left on their sides by the ice. Some valleys have been formed by a sinking of the land between two fractures in the earth's crust. These are usually narrow and long and are known as rift valleys.

Strüktürler: 1. Pres. part. takımı, 2. Past part. sıfatı, 3. Fiilden sonra gelen mastar, 4. Fiil ismi.

BİLGİ YOKLAMASI II

1. BOTANY, FORESTRY

The reproduction of fungi is quite different from the reproduction of other flowering plants. In flowering plants the ovules are fertilised by pollen grain, and from this the seeds are produced. However, a toadstool is not fertilised in this way. On the underside of its cap, tiny spores develop. They are like fine grains of dust, much smaller than any seeds, and millions of them are produced. The spores germinate on suitable ground, and grow as filaments and send out branches. These form a network under the ground and from these the new toadstools develop.

2. ARCHAEOLOGY, HISTORY

The first temple with long rows of columns was dedicated to the goddess Hera, on the island of Samos in about 700 B. C. It was pulled down in 550 B. C. and replaced by a very much larger temple. The Parthenon in Athens was completed in 430 B. C. Inside the temple there was a great statue to the goddess Athene. It was made of gold and ivory and was several times the height of a man. In front was the altar and here, prayers and sacrifices were offered to the goddess. Most Greek temples were built in Doric style and were beautifully decorated with carving.

3. HISTORY, ANTHROPOLOGY, CHEMISTRY

Many of the common ores of metals are oxides, carbonates or sulphides. Copper and tin, the two earliest metals to be smelted by man, are found as oxide ores; that is, the metal is combined with oxygen. This must be removed from the ore to obtain the metal and the simplest way to do this is to heat the ore with carbon. The carbon combines with the oxygen and forms the gas carbon dioxide, leaving the metal behind. Carbon is formed by the burning of wood, so some metal ores, such as copper ore or tin ore, can be converted to the metal by heating in a wood fire. About 6,000 years ago, man discovered this method and copper, the first metal, was obtained. Iron does not melt at such a low temperature and therefore, its ore, is not reduced to the metal as easily as tin or copper. For this reason, men did not obtain iron from iron ore until about 1,500 B.C.

4. MEDICINE, DENTISTRY

Calcium is necessary both for growth and for the maintenance of good health in the body. At least 15 grammes of calcium are required daily, and foods rich in calcium should be included in the diet. The richest sources of calcium are milk, yolk of egg, peas, potato and rice. Bones are formed by cells embedded in an intercellular substance containing calcium in the form of calcium phosphate. This gives the bones their hardness. The substance is built into columns of calcareous material and fibres, and each column contains vessels. This structure makes the bone very strong. The tibia, for example, can support a weight of one and a half tons.

5. CHEMISTRY, PHYSICS

The molecule is the smallest possible particle of a substance. A molecule of salt can be divided into two parts. One is an atom of chlorine and the other is an atom of sodium. Neither of them alone is salt. The water molecule can also be decomposed. It breaks up into three parts: two atoms of hydrogen and one of oxygen. All molecules of water are made like this: In a molecule of marble there is one atom of calcium, one atom of carbon and three atoms of oxygen. All molecules of marble are made like this.

6. MEDICINE, DENTISTRY

Among dental diseases, the most common, especially in children are caries, or cavities in the teeth. The basis of dental hygiene is healthy food, particularly foods rich in vitamin C and mineral salts. Foods containing sugar should be avoided or at least the teeth should be cleaned after eating. Sudden extreme changes in temperature are harmful to teeth, so iced drinks and hot soups should be avoided. Acids form a danger to tooth enamel and destroy the calcium phosphate contained in it. After forming a crack in the enamel, bacteria reach the dentine and tooth decay begins.

7. GEOGRAPHY, GEOLOGY, SCIENCE

Millions of years ago, thick deposits of various materials accumulated on the ocean floor. Mud, sand, vegetable matter, treetrunks and animal remains were carried down to the sea by rivers. Seaweed, fish, molluscs and millions of microscopic creatures living in the sea, were deposited on the ocean floor after their death. The organic substances were then transformed by the action of bacteria. The mass was decomposed into a thick black liquid - crude petroleum. The layers of strata of porous rocks, saturated with petroleum were fractured and folded and raised above sealevel by the action of earthquakes, and other gradual movements of the earth's crust. The petroleum left its original stratum and rose into the dome-shaped rocks and accumulated there. The salt water mixed with it sank, and the lighter petroleum floated on top of the water. The gases produced by the process of decomposition accumulated above the petroleum. In this way, a system of petroleum-bearing strata was formed.

Sözlük

birikmek

layer

(su üstünde) yüzmek

değiştirmek, dönüştürmek

8. GEOGRAPHY, FORESTRY

The mountain helps to increase the fertility of the plain. It causes the humid winds to shed their rain and so protects the plain from excessive moisture. It catches the rain and provides a perpetual supply of water for the crops in the valley below. During the periods of flood, valuable substances are washed down; for example, calcium, potassium and silica. These enrich the soil of the plains.

9. HISTORY, LAW

As yet there was neither political nor religious liberty for the individual. A split between Crown and Parliament might, however, produce both. England was not a despotism. The power of the Crown rested, not on force, but on popular support. The people still wished the Crown to use these powers in the public interest, and the English State had won control of religion from the mediaeval Church.

10. MEDICINE

Gall stones are solid bodies forming in the gall bladder. They vary in size from fragments no bigger than grains of sand to stones the size of a hazel nut. They are usually formed of a mixture of cholesterol, bilirubin and calcium carbonate, but some stones are 'pure' and consist of only one of these substances. Gall stones cannot usually be seen on an X-ray. Their density is not great enough for them to be distinguishable from the surrounding tissue.

11. PHILOSOPHY, PSYCHOLOGY

The principles of behaviour are observed by members of a society to make life more stable and secure. But different societies have widely varied histories and therefore their moral codes of behaviour vary a great deal. Even within the limits of a single social group there may be great differences in the way of life. Barbarian man reserved for himself all functions of government, war, hunting and sport. He left the mechanical functions to women.

12. ECONOMICS, LAW, HISTORY

The years between the wars still provided many great problems. Perhaps the greatest of these was the problem of unemployment. It reached its highest levels during the Great Depression in the thirties. New measures were introduced and new services were provided to care for the unemployed and their families. Sometimes unemployment insurance seemed inadequate and in many cases the amount was increased for families in special circumstances.

13. ECONOMICS

Throughout history merchants have travelled widely all over the world with their goods, and tried to sell them at a profit. In former times most of the buying and selling was carried out at markets. With the profit, the merchant might then buy local goods for sale in some distant market. So the merchants bought and sold and transported goods from town to town and often to distant lands. This ancient method of trade changed with improved communication and now the details of most trade are arranged by correspondence. The merchant dispatches his goods, and these are received and paid for by the buyer without any personal contact.

14. PSYCHOLOGY, PHILOSOPHY

We must try to sum up the practical work with children and their parents in child psychiatry. The first task is to recognise the nature and area of trouble. It is necessary to study in detail the child's behaviour and to investigate his life, background and parent relationship. The second task is to work with the parents and the child and to make the parents aware of the problem and its implications. The child must feel able to accept and be accepted by the doctor and by the parents themselves. Then the third stage is to follow up by working with the child and the parents and to replace the stresses of the presenting situations with confidence and understanding.

15. LAW, ECONOMICS

Rent is the price paid by the tenant for the use of premises, land or house. Rent is usually an agreed sum of money, but a lease may be rent-free or payment may be made in goods or services. According to common law, rent is due to be paid on the last day of a rent interval, but this is usually changed by agreement, to the first day of this interval. Tenancy may be classified as three types: 1) tenancy for years, 2) periodic tenancy and 3) tenancy at will. Tenancy for years includes long-term leases of 99 or 999 years. Periodic tenancies are repeatedly renewed until termination after proper notice. Tenancy at will is an indefinite tenancy and may be terminated by either the landlord or the tenant at any time.

16. LAW

Constitutional law prescribes the method of organisation of government, the obligation of government officers and departments, and limits the powers of the government. International law is concerned with rules regulating the conduct of one nation towards another. It also deals with the conduct of one nation towards the citizen of another. Private law consists of the large number of rules regulating the conduct between private individuals. Administrative law is a new branch of law and deals with the functions of government boards, bureaus and commissions.

17. HISTORY OF ART, LITERATURE

The city of Florence was one of the richest business centres in Italy, and it was at the heart of the Italian Renaissance in art. One of the most important problems of the early Renaissance painters was to find the technical means to express their interest in the real world around them. They had to learn how to draw the human figure by studying anatomy. They had to learn how to show distance. Masaccio's mathematical use of perspective seemed revolutionary to his contemporaries. He was the first man to attempt to draw perspective on scientific principles. With this discovery of the rules of perspective he opened a whole new artistic world.

18. HISTORY, ANTHROPOLOGY, HISTORY OF ART

We have no clear idea about the invention of the wheel. There are drawings and sculptures illustrating wheeled vehicles at about 3,000 B.C., but the wheel was probably invented much earlier than this. The earliest form of wheel was probably a roller under a large tree trunk. The wheel may have been developed from this, but it is not certain. The tools necessary for cutting the rollers into slices did not appear until the Iron Age. The ancient peoples of Mesopotamia and Egypt used light wheeled carts for transporting small objects. Other earlier systems, such as sledges, were used for transporting heavy objects.

19. ASTRONOMY

The earth's atmosphere extends for many thousands of miles as a thin electrified gas of protons and electrons. The region of space influenced by the earth's magnetic field is called the magnetosphere. Beyond this is the solar wind, a continuous stream of hot ionised gas arising from the sun. The wind was first detected by earth satellites and later by interplanetary space-vehicles launched towards the moon and the planet Venus. The wind has a very high velocity, normally about 200 miles per second and may increase to 500 miles per second during solar storms. A very disturbed layer of gas about 100 miles thick is formed at the meeting of the solar wind and the magnetosphere.

20. SCIENCE

Fire is the visible sign of a chemical reaction taking place between fuel and the oxygen of the air. In such a reaction, two substances combine to form one or more new substances. Common fuels, such as wood, coal and petrol, are mainly composed of carbon and hydrogen. On burning, oxygen combines with the carbon to form carbon dioxide, and with the hydrogen to form water. Flame itself consists of glowing particles of carbon rising from the fuel or of dust particles floating in the air. These become red-hot when in contact with the hot gases formed in combustion. Any chemical reaction will take place only if certain conditions are present. For combustion, the necessary condition is heat. The fuel must be brought to a certain temperature, known as the ignition point. With sufficient oxygen, combustion will then take place. Oxygen combines with the fuel and the molecules break down. Energy is released in the form of heat.

Sözlük

İngilizce Kelime

21. SCIENCE

Crystals form in several ways. They usually result from the slow cooling of a molten substance or from the cooling or evaporation of a solution in water or other liquid. Very rarely, crystals are formed directly by the condensation of the vapour of a hot solid. Precious stones are naturally formed crystals and are all formed by the slow crystallisation in the earth's crust of common minerals. Metals are also crystalline in structure. One property is constant in all crystals. This is the angle between the faces of the crystal. Because of this, a mineral can often be identified by measuring the angles between the faces of its crystal.

Sözlük

İngilizce Kelime

Bileşik Cümleler

Bileşik cümle, bir (veya birden fazla) bağımsız (ana) cümle ile bir (veya birden fazla) bağımlı cümlecikten oluşur. Bağımlı cümleciğin 3 türlüsü vardır: Zarf, Sıfat ve İsim Cümleciği. Her cümleciğin öznesi ve çekimli fiili vardır. Bileşik cümleyi anlamak veya tercüme etmek için bağımlı ve bağımsız (ana) cümlecikleri birbirinden ayırıp önce bağımlı, sonra bağımsız (ana) cümleciği yerleştirmelidir. İngilizcede bağımlı cümlecik, hem ana cümlecikten önce hem de sonra bulunabilir. Türkçede büyük ekseriyetle, bağımlı cümlecik önce gelir.

Sayfa 164

I. ZARF CÜMLECİKLERİ

Zarf cümleciği daima bir zarf olan işaret kelimesiyle başlar. Bu işaret kelimelerinin anlamını bilmek lazımdır. Ona göre zarf cümlecikte bulunan fiile uygun bir şekil verilir. En mutad işaret kelimeleri Zaman, Sebep, Maksat, Netice, Şart veya Derece bildirirler. Bunların en mühimleri sıra ile aşağıda ele alınmaktadır.

1. Zaman Zarfıyla Başlayan Zarf Cümleciği

En mühim işaret kelimeleri şunlardır:

a) before: etmeden (önce, evvel)

b) after: ettikten sonra

c) when: edince (Sayfa 172'ye bakınız)

d) since: edeli, ettiğinden beri

e) while / as: ederken

f) until: edinceye kadar

a) Before

Alıştırma 127

Örnek: Before we go home ((Biz) eve gitmeden önce)

Aşağıda verilmiş "before" ile başlayan zarf cümleciklerinin fiilleri edilgen şeklinde bulunuyor. Zamana göre Türkçeye çeviriniz:

before the reaction had been observed (reaksiyon gözetlenmiş olmadan)

1. before the substance is dissolved

2. before the substance had been obtained

3. before fire had been invented

4. before fire was invented

5. before the substance is heated

6. before the law was passed

7. before the people had been civilised

8. before coal was used

9. before the proposal was considered

10. before this method was used

11. before the new methods had been introduced

12. before coal was discovered in the area

13. before the factory was built

14. before the results are published

15. before the substance is heated

16. before impurities are removed

17. before the oil is refined

18. before the disease had been treated

19. before the trees are planted

20. before the suggestion was accepted by the committee

Alıştırma 131

Aşağıda yazılmış olan cümlelerdeki zarf cümleciklerini kerre içine alarak başa getirip tercüme ettikten sonra kalan ana cümleciklerini tercüme ediniz:

Örnek: We must finish the work [before we go home]. ([Eve gitmeden] işi bitirmeliyiz.)

1. There is a lot to do before our aims are accomplished.

2. We must collect more information before we can act.

Sayfa 167

3. The machine must be adjusted before it can be used.

4. The armies rested for a day before they advanced towards the city.

5. The armies rested for a day before they approached the river.

6. We must learn about the nature of molecules before we study the behaviour of liquids.

7. We must study the arrangement of the molecules before we can understand the transference of heat in a metal.

8. The supply of raw materials must be increased before the demand for these articles can be met.

9. A seed must absorb water before it can germinate.

10. The cooperation of the workers must be obtained before new methods can be introduced.

2. Before our aims can be accomplished, there is a great deal of work to do.

3. Before we can take any action in the matter, we must collect more information.

4. Before computers were introduced into the banks, there was much more delay in business.

5. Before they approached the city, the army rested for a few days.

6. Before the army advanced to the river, it rested for a day.

7. Before we study the behaviour of liquids, we must study the nature of molecules.

8. Before we can understand the transference of heat in a metal, we must learn about the arrangement of molecules.

9. Before a seed can germinate, it absorbs a certain amount of water.

10. Before new methods can be introduced into the factory, the cooperation of the workers must be obtained.

Alıştırma 135

Aşağıda verilmiş olan cümlelerdeki zarf cümleciklerini kerre içine alıp cümleleri tercüme ediniz:

Örnek: After the army had rested it advanced to the city. (Ordu, istirahat ettikten sonra şehre doğru ilerledi.)

1. There will be less work to do after computers have been introduced into the banks.

2. Action can be taken after available information has been collected.

3. After the machine has been adjusted it can be used for making these measurements.

4. After they had rested for a few days the armies advanced towards the city.

5. After they had rested for a day the armies approached the river.

6. We can study the nature of liquids after we have learned about the behaviour of molecules.

7. After we have studied the arrangement of molecules we can understand the transference of heat in a metal.

8. Only after the supply of raw materials has been increased can we meet the demand for these goods.

9. After a seed has absorbed water it swells.

10. Improvements can be introduced after their purpose has been explained to the workers in the factory.

c) When

"When" ile başlayan zarf cümleciğinin tercümesi, cümlecikteki fiilin zamanına göre değişir:

i) Fiil, ŞİMDİKİ zamanda ise, Türkçede GELECEK zaman ile yahut "-de, -da" takısı ile tercüme edilir:

Örnek: When he comes (geleceği zaman, geldiğinde)

When it starts (başlayacağı zaman, başladığında)

ii) Fiil, GEÇMİŞ zamanda ise, "-de, -da" veya "-ce, -ca" takısı ile tercüme edilir:

Örnek: When he came (geldiğinde, gelince)

When it started (başladığında, başlayınca)

iii) Fiil, PRESENT/PAST PERFECT zamanda ise, "-tikten sonra" diye tercüme edilir:

Örnek: When he has come (geldikten sonra)

When it had started (başladıktan sonra)

iv) Fiil, EDİLGEN kipinde ise, "-de, -da" takısı ile tercüme edilir:

Örnek: When it is done (yapıldığında)

When they were taken (alındıklarında)

v) Fiil, EDİLGEN, PAST PERFECT zamanda ise, "-ilmiş olduktan sonra" diye tercüme edilir:

Örnek: When it had been done (yapılmış olduktan sonra)

When they had been taken (alınmış olduktan sonra)

Yukarıda verilen beş noktalı açıklamaya göre aşağıda yazılmış olan alıştırmaları yapınız.

Alıştırma 142: a)

Aşağıda yazılmış olan cümlelerdeki zarf cümleciklerini kerre içine alıp ayrı olarak tercüme ettikten sonra kalan ana cümlelerine bağlayarak bütün cümleyi tercüme ediniz:

1. When the heat of the sun melts the snow, the water penetrates into the cracks in the rocks.

2. When darkness falls, the process of photosynthesis ceases.

3. When light falls upon certain chemical compounds of silver, they turn darker in colour.

4. When we breathe in, the chest cavity becomes bigger.

5. When we breathe out, the chest cavity becomes smaller.

6. When the embryo of a seed begins to grow, it feeds on the nutrients in the seed.

7. When water freezes, it increases its volume by about ten percent.

8. When the temperature falls at night, the water in the cracks of the rocks freezes.

Alıştırma 142: b)

Şimdi aynı cümleler aşağıda verilmiştir; bu sefer önce ana cümlecik, sonra zarf cümleciği sıralanmıştır. Zarf cümleciğini başa yerleştirip bütün cümleyi tercüme ediniz:

1. The water penetrates into the cracks of the rocks when the heat of the sun melts the snow.

2. The process of photosynthesis ceases when darkness falls.

3. Certain chemical compounds of silver turn darker in colour when light falls upon them.

4. The chest cavity becomes larger when we breathe in.

5. The chest cavity becomes smaller when we breathe out.

6. The embryo of a seed feeds on the nutrients in the seed when it begins to grow.

Sayfa 177

7. Water increases its volume by about ten per cent when it freezes.

8. The water in the cracks of the rocks freezes when the temperature falls at night.

Anlama Soruları

A.

1. When does the water penetrate into the cracks of the rocks?

2. When does the process of photosynthesis cease?

3. When do certain chemical compounds of silver turn darker in colour?

4. When does the chest cavity become larger?

5. When does the chest cavity become smaller?

6. When does the embryo of a seed feed on the nutrients in the seed?

7. When does water increase its volume by about ten per cent?

8. When does the water in the cracks of the rocks freeze?

B.

1. What happens when the heat of the sun melts the snow?

2. What happens when darkness falls?

3. What happens when light falls on certain chemical compounds?

4. What happens when we breathe in?

5. What happens when we breathe out?

6. What happens when the embryo of a seed begins to grow?

7. What happens when water freezes?

8. What happens when the temperature falls at night?

C.

1. Where does the water penetrate?

2. What ceases when darkness falls?

3. What turn darker in colour when light falls on them?

4. What becomes bigger when we breathe in?

5. What becomes smaller when we breathe out?

6. On what does the embryo of a seed feed when it begins to grow?

7. By how much is the volume of water increased when it freezes?

8. What freezes when the temperature falls at night?

Alıştırmalar

Alıştırma 143: a)

Aşağıda yazılmış olan cümlelerdeki "when" zarf cümleciklerini kerre içine alıp ayrı olarak tercüme ettikten sonra, kalan ana cümleciklerine bağlayarak bütün cümleyi tercüme ediniz:

1. The committee will submit a report when it has collected all the available information.

2. The plant can absorb more water and nutrients when the roots have developed.

3. More goods can be imported when the market has grown.

Sayfa 178

4. The tissues must be removed as soon as possible when they have become diseased.

5. The rivers often break their banks when heavy rains have fallen.

6. The water level in the rivers rises when the snow in the mountains has melted.

7. A vote will be taken when the committee have discussed the matter.

8. When the substance has been dried, it is weighed.

Alıştırma 143: b)

Şimdi aynı cümleler aşağıda verilmiştir; bu sefer önce zarf cümleciği, sonra ana cümleciği sıralanmıştır. Zarf cümleciğini kerre içine aldıktan sonra tercüme edip ana cümleciğiyle beraber Türkçeye çeviriniz:

1. When the committee has collected all the available information, it will submit a report.

2. When the roots have developed, the plant can absorb more water and nutrients.

3. When the market has grown, more goods can be imported.

4. When the tissues have become diseased, they must be removed as soon as possible.

5. When heavy rains have fallen, the rivers often break their banks.

6. When the snow in the mountains has melted, the water level in the rivers rises.

7. When the committee have discussed the matter, a vote will be taken.

8. When the substance has been dried, it is weighed.

Anlama Soruları

A.

1. When will the committee submit a report?

2. When can the plant absorb more water and nutrients?

3. When can more goods be imported?

4. When must the tissues be removed as soon as possible?

Sayfa 179

5. When do rivers often break their banks?

6. When does the water level in the rivers rise?

7. When will a vote be taken?

8. When is the substance weighed?

B.

1. When the committee has collected all the available information, what will it do?

2. When the roots have developed what can the plant do?

3. When the market has grown what can be done?

4. When the tissues have become diseased what must be done?

5. When heavy rains have fallen what do the rivers often do?

6. When the snow in the mountains has melted, what happens?

7. When the committee have discussed the matter what will be done?

8. When the substance has been dried what is done?

C.

1. What will the committee submit?

2. What can the plant absorb?

3. What can be imported?

4. What must be removed?

5. What do rivers often break?

6. What rises?

7. What will be taken?

8. What is weighed?

1. Metal contracts when it is cooled.

2. The reforms will be introduced when the new government is established.

3. Water turns carbon dioxide into soluble bicarbonate when it is mixed.

4. Sugar is decomposed and combined with oxygen when it is consumed to provide muscle with energy.

5. Metal expands when it is heated.

6. A solution is formed when the substance is dissolved in water.

Alıştırma 144: b)

Şimdi aynı cümleler aşağıda verilmiştir; bu sefer önce zarf cümleciği sıralanmıştır. Evvelki alıştırmada yaptığınız gibi Türkçeye çeviriniz:

1. When it is cooled metal contracts.

2. When the new government is established the reforms will be introduced.

3. When water is mixed with carbon dioxide it turns it into soluble bicarbonate.

4. When sugar is consumed to provide muscle with energy it is decomposed and combined with oxygen.

5. When metal is heated it expands.

6. When the substance is dissolved in water a solution is formed.

7. When the logs are cut the timber is transported to the mill.

8. When the bacteria are examined under the microscope they can be identified.

A.

4. When is sugar decomposed and combined with oxygen?

5. When does metal expand?

6. When is a solution formed?

7. When is timber transported to the mill?

8. When can the bacteria be identified?

B.

1. What happens when metal is cooled?

2. What will be introduced?

3. What happens when water is mixed with carbon dioxide?

4. What happens when sugar is consumed to provide muscle with energy?

5. What happens when metal is heated?

6. What is formed when a substance is dissolved in water?

7. Where is timber transported when the logs are cut?

8. What can be done when the bacteria are examined under a microscope?

d) 'Since' ile Başlayan Zaman Zarf Cümleciği

Tercümesi "...-den beri" veya "-eli / -alı" şeklinde olur:

Örnek: It is a long time since his mother died. (Annesinin ölümünden beri çok zaman geçti. / Annesi öleli çok zaman geçti.)

Sayfa 181

Alıştırma 145

Aşağıda verilen "since" zaman zarf cümleciklerini kerre içine alıp örnekte gösterildiği gibi tercüme ettikten sonra kalan ana cümleciğine bağlayıp Türkçeye çeviriniz:

1. It is not long since the new law was passed.

2. The young plants have grown six inches since they were planted.

3. The children have learnt to read and write since they started school last September.

4. The committee has not held any meetings since the new president was elected.

5. The law has not been altered in any way since it was first passed 100 years ago.

6. Work has been greatly facilitated since electronic equipment has been installed.

7. The quality of these goods has been inferior since the new methods of manufacture have been used.

8. The prosperity of the district has greatly increased since the large iron and steel factories have been opened.

Sözlük

İngilizce Kelime

Türkçe Anlamı

to alter

değiştirmek

committee

heyet, kurul, komite

district

seçmek

equipment

tesisat, donanım, ekipman

kolaylaştırmak

factory

fabrika

to hold a meeting

to install

iron

to pass (a law)

plant

to plant

dikmek

prosperity

refah, zenginlik

quality

kalite, nitelik

steel

çelik

Anlama Soruları

A.

1. What is not long?

2. When have the young plants grown six inches?

3. When have the children learnt to read and write?

4. When has the committee not held any meetings?

5. When has the new law not been altered in any way?

6. When has work been greatly facilitated?

7. When has the quality of these goods been inferior?

8. When has the prosperity of the district increased?

Sayfa 182

B.

1. What was passed not long ago?

2. How much have the plants grown?

3. What have the children learnt to do?

4. What has the committee not done since the new president was elected?

5. What has not been altered in any way?

6. What has been greatly facilitated?

7. What has happened to the quality of these goods?

8. What has greatly increased since the large iron and steel factories have been opened?

e) 'While' ve 'as' ile Başlayan Zaman Zarf Cümleciklerinin Tercümesi

Tercümesi "-dikçe" veya "-iken" şeklinde olur:

Örnek: Our experience grows as we learn. (Öğrendikçe tecrübemiz artar.)

They poured water onto the house while it was burning. (Ev yanıyorken üstüne su döküyorlardı.)

Alıştırma 147

Aşağıda verilmiş olan "as" veya "while" cümlelerini örnekte gösterildiği gibi Türkçeye çeviriniz:

1. The various organs of a seed are developed while the seed grows.

2. We can expect the quality of goods to improve as our experience of production grows.

3. While they were making a study of the behaviour of a certain virus, they discovered new facts about the structure of the cell.

4. While wages are low and conditions of work are bad, health is an important factor in society.

5. The photographic plate must be exposed while it is still wet.

6. Educationists should teach their pupils to appreciate the beauty of life while they are still young.

7. Thousands of bacteria find a suitable environment for their growth as the wood decays.

8. A lot can be learned by limiting the experiences of an animal as it grows up.

9. As wood decays thousands of bacteria find it suitable for their growth.

10. As we trace life back to its early beginning on earth we can observe two qualities common to all forms of life.

11. As water passes over the rocks it wears away the surface.

12. The cells of the blood float about in the fluid part of the blood as it circulates in the body.

f) 'Until' ile Başlayan Zarf Cümleciğinin Tercümesi

Tercümesi, örnekte gösterildiği gibi "...-ceye kadar" kalıbı kullanarak yapılır:

Örnek: They could not leave until the storm was over. (Fırtına geçinceye kadar ayrılamadılar.)

Sayfa 185

Alıştırma 148

Aşağıda verilmiş olan "until" ile başlayan zarf cümleciklerini Türkçeye çeviriniz:

1. until it is dry

2. until it is hard

3. until it is soft

4. until it is ready

5. until it is finished

6. until it was empty

7. until it is full

8. until it is necessary

9. until it disappears

10. until it changes

11. until it develops

12. until it gets better

13. until it dies

14. until it ripens

15. until it improves

16. until it melts

17. until it evaporates

18. until it has been considered

19. until it had been completed

20. until it had been introduced

Alıştırma 149: a)

Aşağıda verilmiş olan cümlelerin zarf cümleciklerini kerre içine aldıktan sonra kalan ana cümleciğine bağlayıp tercüme ediniz:

1. The piston was held up until the cylinder cooled.

2. The functions of government cannot be carried out properly until all the members are educated and experienced.

3. No great advance in the study of anatomy was made until dissections were carried out in the medieval universities.

4. Antibodies are not produced naturally until the body is attacked by bacteria.

5. The establishment of schools was left to religious bodies or private groups until education became a public service in Britain.

6. No real practical use could be made of Galileo's compound microscope until German and British technicians in the 19th century could make satisfactory lenses.

Alıştırma 149: b)

Şimdi aynı cümlelerde, zarf cümlecikleri ana cümlelerden önce yerleştirilmiştir. Aynı şekilde Türkçeye çeviriniz:

1. Until the cylinder was cooled, the piston was held up.

2. Until all the members are educated and experienced, the functions of government cannot be carried out properly.

3. Until dissections were carried out in the medieval universities, no great advance in the study of anatomy was made.

Sayfa 186

4. Until the body is attacked by bacteria antibodies are not produced naturally.

5. Until education became a public service in Britain, the establishment of schools was left to religious bodies or private groups.

6. Until German and British technicians in the nineteenth century could make satisfactory lenses, no real practical use could be made of Galileo's compound microscope.

Sözlük

Anlama Soruları

A.

1. Until when was the piston held up?

2. Until when cannot the functions of government be carried out properly?

3. Until when was no great advance made in the study of anatomy?

4. Until when are antibodies not produced naturally?

5. Until when was the establishment of schools left to religious bodies or private groups?

6. Until when could not real practical use be made of Galileo's compound microscope?

B.

1. What was done until the cylinder cooled?

2. What cannot be carried out properly until all the members are educated and experienced?

3. What was not made until dissections were carried out in the medieval universities?

4. What is not done until the body is attacked by bacteria?

Sayfa 187

5. What was done until education became a public service in Britain?

6. What could not be done until German and British technicians in the 19th century could make satisfactory lenses?

B. Sebep Gösteren Zarf Cümleciği

En mühim işaret kelimeleri şunlardır:

because / as / since : -olduğundan, olduğu için, -dolayısıyla, olmasından, çünkü, zira

Tercümesi, yukarıda gösterildiği gibi, birkaç şekilde olur.

a) 'Because' ile Başlayan Zarf Cümleciği

Alıştırmalar

Alıştırma 150

Aşağıda yazılan "because" ile başlayan zarf cümleciklerini Türkçeye çeviriniz:

1. because it was proved

2. because it was published

3. because it is known

4. because it is purified

5. because it has been increased

6. because it has been formed

7. because it had been stated

8. because it had been allowed

9. because it had been cooled

10. because it had been civilised

11. because it had been decided

12. because it is applied

13. because it is obtained

14. because it has been demonstrated

15. because it is included

16. because it was influenced

17. because it has been said

18. because it is required

19. because it is produced

20. because it was selected

İngilizce Kelime

Türkçe Anlamı

to allow

Alıştırma 151: a)

Aşağıda verilmiş olan cümlelerin zarf cümleciklerini kerre içine aldıktan sonra, yukarıda gösterildiği gibi tercüme ediniz. Sonra kalan ana cümleye bağlayıp bütün cümleyi Türkçeye çeviriniz:

1. Because machines are used, America can produce a large quantity and variety of goods.

2. Because the population increased rapidly in England between 1700 and 1800, there was plenty of labour for the new factories.

Sayfa 188

3. Because Britain had sources of power, such as water and coal, the Industrial Revolution was greatly assisted in Britain.

4. Because Britain had an effective central government, the Industrial Revolution could take place in Britain more easily.

5. Because communities became too big to be managed by primitive tribal methods, it became more difficult to organise life in a community.

6. Because the new factories of the 19th century needed literate workers to run the machines, the government began to finance elementary schools.

7. Because the retina of man's eyes is not like the retina of reptiles and birds, man developed colour vision.

8. Because the soil is too compact, the root system of the young plant cannot develop properly.

9. Because it allowed him to share ideas and plan together, the ability to speak was of great value to early Man.

10. Because he can do so many different things with his limbs, Man is the most skilful of all living things.

11. Because Man lacked the means of finding out the truth, unreasonable ideas about the causes of disease were preserved.

12. Because few people were left to plant and harvest crops, famine nearly always followed the plague. Because it killed so high a proportion of the population the plague stopped the Hundred Years' War in 1350.

13. Because the cause was not understood, all methods to prevent the spread of infection failed.

14. Because he could not discover the true cause of infectious illness, Man had no chance of controlling disease before the invention of the microscope.

Alıştırma 151: b)

Şimdi aynı cümleler aşağıda yazılmıştır. Bu sefer önce ana cümlecik, sonra zarf cümleciği sıralanmıştır. Yukarıdaki gibi, ayrı ayrı tercüme edip birbirine bağlayarak Türkçeye çeviriniz:

1. The Industrial Revolution was greatly assisted in Britain because Britain had sources of power, such as water and coal.

2. There was plenty of labour for the new factories because the population increased rapidly in England between 1700 and 1800.

3. America can produce a large quantity and variety of goods because machines are used.

4. The Industrial Revolution could take place in Britain more easily because Britain had an effective central government.

5. It became more difficult to organise life in communities because they became too big to be managed by primitive tribal methods.

6. The government began to finance elementary schools because the new factories of the 19th century needed literate workers to run the machines.

7. Man developed colour vision because the retina of man's eyes is not like the retina of reptiles and birds.

8. The root system of the young plant cannot develop properly because the soil is too compact.

9. The ability to speak was of great value to early Man because it allowed him to share ideas and plan together.

10. Man is the most skilful of all living things because he can do so many different things with his limbs.

Sayfa 190

11. Unreasonable ideas about the causes of disease were preserved because Man lacked the means of finding out the truth.

12. Famine nearly always followed the plague because few people were left to plant and harvest the crops. The plague stopped the Hundred Years' War in 1350 because it killed so high a proportion of the population.

13. All methods to prevent the spread of infection failed because the cause was not understood.

14. Man had no chance of controlling disease before the invention of the microscope, because he could not discover the true cause of infectious illness.

Anlama Soruları

A.

1. Why was the Industrial Revolution greatly assisted in Britain?

2. Why was there plenty of labour for the new factories?

3. Why can America produce a large quantity and variety of goods?

4. Why could the Industrial Revolution take place in Britain more easily?

5. Why did it become more difficult to organise life in a community?

6. Why did the government begin to finance elementary schools?

7. Why did man develop colour vision?

8. Why cannot the root system of the young plant develop properly?

9. Why was the ability to speak of great value to man?

10. Why is man the most skilful of all living things?

11. Why were unreasonable ideas about the causes of disease preserved?

12. Why did famine nearly always follow plague? Why did the plague stop the Hundred Years' War?

13. Why did all methods to prevent the spread of infection fail?

14. Why had Man no chance of controlling disease before the invention of the microscope?

B.

1. Give two examples of Britain's sources of power.

2. What was there?

3. What can America do?

4. What could take place more easily in Britain?

5. What became more difficult to manage?

6. What did the new factories of the 19th century need?

7. What did man develop?

8. What cannot develop properly?

9. What was of great value to early man?

10. Who is the most skilful of all living things?

Sayfa 191

11. Which unreasonable ideas were preserved?

12. What nearly always followed plague? What did the plague do in 1350?

13. What failed?

14. What had Man no chance of doing?

b) 'Since' ile Başlayan Sebep Gösteren Zarf Cümleciği

Alıştırmalar

Alıştırma 152

Aşağıda verilmiş cümleleri, yukarıda olan "because" cümleleri gibi Türkçeye çeviriniz:

1. Since RNA and DNA carry the knowledge needed for regeneration we call them genetic substances.

2. Since water increases its volume by about 10 per cent when it freezes, the ice caused a great pressure inside the crack.

3. Since American society is a machine society it can produce large quantities and varieties of goods.

4. Since the population increased rapidly in Britain during the 18th century there was plenty of labour available for the new factories.

5. Since Britain had large sources of power, such as coal and water the Industrial Revolution took place more easily in Britain.

6. Since there were highly organised financial institutions, such as the Bank of England and the Stock Exchange, the Industrial Revolution could take place more easily in Britain.

7. Since communities rapidly increased in size, they became too big to be managed by primitive tribal methods.

8. Since the soil had become too hard and dry, the roots of the young plants could not develop quickly.

9. Since the building of a bridge across the river will cost a great deal of money, the government is unwilling to undertake the enterprise.

10. Since most of the land is cultivated for food crops, very little of it can be planted with trees.

c) 'As' ile Başlayan Sebep Gösteren Zarf Cümleciği

Alıştırmalar

Alıştırma 153: a)

Aşağıda verilen cümleleri, yukarıda görülmüş olan "because" veya "since" ile başlayan cümleler gibi Türkçeye çeviriniz:

1. As the patient was suffering from high blood pressure, doctors were unwilling to perform the operation.

2. As the population had increased very rapidly between 1700 and 1800, plenty of labour was available for the new factories.

Sayfa 193

3. As the cost of production and raw materials is too great, the annual profits cannot be very high.

4. As a large amount of capital expenditure would be required, the introduction of modern machinery must be delayed at present.

5. As the evidence is not sufficient to prove the theory, further experiments must be carried out.

6. As the substance was not weighed carefully before and after drying, the experiment has no value.

7. As dangerous materials are being handled in this factory, special protective clothing must be worn by all the workers.

8. As Switzerland is never involved in European wars, the Zurich banks hold large amounts of money for customers all over the world.

9. As the roots are dormant during the winter, plants do not carry out their function of absorbing water during this season.

10. As animals eat ready-made organic substances and as plants make their own organic substances, there is a great difference in the feeding method of plants and animals.

Alıştırma 153: b)

Yine yukarıdaki cümleler aşağıda verilmiştir. Bu sefer önce ana cümle, sonra zarf cümlecikleri sıralanmıştır. Türkçeye çeviriniz:

1. Doctors were unwilling to perform the operation as the patient was suffering from high blood pressure.

2. Plenty of labour was available for the new factories as the population in Britain increased rapidly between 1700 and 1800.

Sayfa 194

3. The annual profits cannot be very high, as the cost of production and raw materials is too great.

4. The introduction of modern machinery must be delayed at present, as a large amount of capital expenditure would be required.

5. Further experiments must be carried out as the evidence is not sufficient to prove the theory.

6. The experiment has no value as the substance was not weighed carefully before and after drying.

7. Special protective clothing must be worn by all the workers as dangerous materials are being handled in this factory.

8. The Zurich banks hold large amounts of money for customers all over the world, as Switzerland is never involved in European wars.

9. Plants do not carry out their function of absorbing water during the winter as the roots are dormant during this season.

10. There is a great difference in the feeding methods of plants and animals as animals eat ready-made organic substances and plants make their own organic substances.

Anlama Soruları

A.

1. Why were doctors unwilling to perform the operation?

2. Why was plenty of labour available for the new factories?

3. Why cannot the annual profits be very high?

4. Why must the introduction of modern machinery be delayed at present?

5. Why must further experiments be carried out?

6. Why must special protective clothing be worn by all the workers?

7. Why has the experiment no value?

8. Why do Zurich banks hold large sums of money for customers all over the world?

9. Why do not plants carry out their function of absorbing water in winter?

10. Why is there a great difference in the feeding methods of plants and animals?

C. 'Although' ile Başlayan Zarf Cümleciği

Örnek: Although he was very ill, he refused to see a doctor. (Çok hasta olmasına rağmen / Çok hasta olduğu halde doktora görünmeyi reddetti.)

Alıştırma 155: a)

Aşağıda verilmiş olan cümlelerin zarf cümleciklerini kerre içine alıp Türkçeye çevirdikten sonra kalan ana cümleye bağlayarak tercüme ediniz:

1. Although a seed may appear to be dry, it contains a little water.

2. Although a great part of the atmosphere consists of nitrogen it cannot be used by plants and animals in its pure form.

3. Although man is naturally strong, disease and starvation kill thousands every year.

4. Although we are alive and although living things are all around us, we do not yet understand the nature of life itself.

5. Although the first lens magnified one hundred times the natural size, bacteria still looked very tiny.

6. Although wheat is grown in some areas, the sub-continent of India is a great rice-growing area.

7. Although one may be derived from the other, matter and energy cannot be created or destroyed.

8. Although the cost of raw materials has increased, we hope to pay for it by increasing exports to the Far East.

9. Although a catalyst accelerates a chemical reaction, it does not itself suffer any change in the process.

10. Although certain chemical reactions will not take place without a catalyst, the catalyst itself does not suffer any change during the reaction.

11. Although the earth's crust is rarely absolutely motionless, most earthquakes today occur only in certain belts.

Alıştırma 155: b)

Yukarıda bulunan cümleler tekrar aşağıda verilmiştir. Bu sefer ana cümlecik başa konmuştur. "Although" cümleciğini başa getirerek Türkçeye çeviriniz:

1. A seed contains a little water although it may appear to be dry.

[Metnin bu bölümü burada sona ermektedir.]

Sağlanan metin, OCR hatalarından ve sayfa yapısındaki bozukluklardan tamamen arındırılarak, orijinal içeriğe (cümleler, anlama soruları, sözlükler, açıklamalar ve sayfa numaraları) sadık kalınacak şekilde sayfa sayfa şu şekilde düzenlenmiştir:

Sayfa 197

Nitrogen cannot be used by plants and animals in its pure form although a great part of the atmosphere consists of this gas.

Disease and starvation kill thousands of men every year although man is naturally strong.

We do not yet understand the nature of life itself although we are alive and although living things are all around us.

Bacteria still looked very tiny although the first lens magnified one hundred times the natural size.

The sub-continent of India is a great rice-growing area although wheat is grown in some areas.

Matter and energy cannot be created or destroyed although one may be derived from the other.

We hope to pay for the increased cost by increasing exports to the Far East although the cost of raw materials has increased.

A catalyst does not itself suffer any change in the process although it accelerates a chemical reaction.

The catalyst itself does not suffer any change during the reaction although certain chemical reactions will not take place without it.

Most earthquakes today occur only in certain belts, although the earth's crust is rarely absolutely motionless.

The underground movement of great masses of molten magma are very important although it cannot be observed at the surface.

Any mineral deficiencies can be remedied by balanced manuring although the chemical composition of the soil is important.

The snow remains on the ground for at least six months of the year in Tibet, although it is further south than the sub-tropical island of Sicily.

Other Europeans visited Asia before Marco Polo although we know very little definite about them.

Anlama soruları

A.

A seed contains a little water, although what?

Nitrogen cannot be used by plants and animals in its pure form although what?

Disease and starvation kill thousands every year although what?

We do not yet understand the nature of life although what?

Bacteria still looked very tiny although what?

The sub-continent of India is a great rice-growing area, although what?

Matter and energy cannot be created or destroyed although what?

Sayfa 198

We hope to pay for the cost of raw materials by increasing exports to the Far East although what?

A catalyst does not itself suffer any change in the process although what?

The catalyst itself does not suffer any change during the reaction although what?

Most earthquakes today occur only in certain belts although what?

The underground movement of great masses of molten magma are very important although what?

Any mineral deficiencies can be remedied by balanced manuring although what?

The snow remains on the ground for at least six months of the year in Tibet although what?

Other Europeans visited Asia before Marco Polo although what?

B.

What does a seed contain?

What cannot plants and animals do?

What do disease and starvation do every year?

What do we not yet understand?

How much did the first lens magnify?

D. Derece tayin eden zarf cümleciği: 'so ... that'

so ... that (o kadar ... ki) ile başlıyor.

Örnek: Cells are so small that they cannot be seen without a microscope.

Hücreler o kadar küçüktür ki mikroskopsuz görülemez.

Alıştırmalar

156. Aşağıda verilmiş olan cümlelerin 'so...that' zarf cümleciğini kerre içine alın, tercüme ediniz. Sonra kalan kısma bağlayıp bütün cümleyi Türkçeye çeviriniz:

The production of cotton increased so rapidly that by 1830 half of Great Britain's exports consisted of cotton.

Sayfa 199

Cells are so tiny that they cannot be seen with the naked eye.

Rabbits became so numerous in Australia that they caused millions of pounds of damage every year.

So many people died of plague in London that it was impossible to bury them in the normal way.

The friction was so great that the engine was not strong enough to move the load.

The capital of this company has been increased so much that modern machinery can now be introduced into its factories.

In winter the snow is so deep that birds cannot dig down into the soil.

Cost of production and raw materials is so high that the annual profit is very small.

The soil was so hard and dry that the water could not penetrate the surface.

The cold during the first weeks of March was so intense that the development of the buds on fruit trees was delayed by at least three weeks.

In sandy soils water may drain away so rapidly that shallow-rooted plants may be left dry.

Clay itself is so fine grained that it acts almost as a colloid.

Repeated ploughing, especially in tropical countries, promotes oxidation so much that good soil has been ruined in a short time.

The rivers in the north flow so rapidly that they are not practicable for navigation.

In a desert the extremes of temperature are so great that the rocks disintegrate very rapidly.

Sözlük

capital: sermaye, anapara

to cause: sebep olmak, neden olmak

cell: hücre

clay: kil

company: şirket

to consist of: -den ibaret olmak

cost: masraf, maliyet

cotton: pamuk

damage: zarar, hasar

to delay: geciktirmek

desert: çöl

development: gelişme

to dig: kazmak

to disintegrate: parçalanmak

to drain away: süzülüp gitmek, akıp gitmek

engine: motor

especially: bilhassa, özellikle

export: ihracat, dışsatım

extreme: uç, ekstrem

fine-grained: ince taneli

to flow: akmak

friction: sürtünme

to increase: artmak, artırmak

intense: şiddetli, yoğun

to introduce: takdim etmek, getirmek

load: yük

naked: çıplak

navigation: gemi seferi, seyrüsefer

numerous: çok, çok sayıda

to penetrate: işlemek, nüfuz etmek

Sayfa 200

plague: veba

production: imalat, üretim

profit: kâr, kazanç

rabbit: tavşan

repeated: tekrarlanan, tekrar tekrar

rock: kaya

to ruin: mahvetmek, bozmak

sandy: kumlu

shallow: sığ

surface: yüzey

tiny: ufacık, çok küçük

Anlama soruları

A.

How rapidly did the production of cotton increase?

How tiny are cells?

To what degree did rabbits become numerous in Australia?

To what extent did people die of plague in London?

How great was the friction?

To what extent is the snow deep?

How hard and dry was the soil?

To what extent may water drain away on sandy soils?

How fine-grained is clay itself?

To what degree does repeated ploughing promote oxidation?

To what extent are the extremes of temperature in a desert great?

What increased rapidly in Britain in 1830?

Sayfa 201

C.

What caused half of Great Britain's exports to consist of cotton in 1830?

Why cannot cells be seen with the naked eye?

Why did rabbits cause millions of pounds of damage every year in Australia?

Why was it impossible to bury people in the normal way?

Why was the engine not strong enough to move the load?

How is it that modern machinery can now be introduced?
