VI. It + to be + sıfat / past part. + mastar + that İle Başlayan İsim Cümleciği

Örnek: It was not easy to see that he was tired.

$$\text{Onun yorgun olduğunu görmek kolay değildi.}$$

It must be difficult to say that you have no money.

$$\text{Paranız olmadığını söylemek güç bir şey olmalıdır.}$$

It is true to say that certain microbes can live without oxygen.

$$\text{Muayyen mikropların oksijensiz yaşayabildiklerini söylemek doğrudur.}$$

--- SAYFA 255 ---

NOT: Cümlenin tercüme edilmesinde güçlüğe uğranılırsa, 'that'den sonra gelen parçayı (yani, isim cümleciğini) ayrı olarak, normal bir ana cümle gibi düşününüz. Sonra mastara kadar gelen parçayı ayrı olarak tercüme ediniz.

Örnek: It is true to say that green plants have the power to purify the air by removing the carbon dioxide from it.

'that'den sonra gelen parça: (green plants have the power to purify the air by removing the carbon dioxide from it.)  Yeşil bitkiler, karbon dioksidi uzaklaştırmakla havayı saflaştırmak kudretine sahiptir.

Mastara kadar gelen parça: (It is true to say)  Söylemek doğrudur.

Beraber koyunca:

$$\text{Yeşil bitkilerin, karbon dioksidi uzaklaştırmakla havayı saflaştırmak kudretine sahip olduklarını söylemek doğrudur.}$$

Alıştırma

191. Yukarıda örnek ve açıklamaya göre aşağıda yazılan cümleleri Türkçeye çeviriniz:

It was easy to see that the forests in these areas would not survive for long.

It is possible to prove that nothing can travel faster than electro-magnetic waves.

It was not difficult to show that goats were one of the main causes of forest devastation in Mediterranean countries.

It is useless to maintain that freedom can exist without a degree of discipline.

It has never been possible to prove that this continent ever existed.

It is useful for educationists to know that group activities become difficult with more than 20 and less than 5 individuals.

It is surprising to learn that the percentage of children attending school has dropped in recent years.

It was interesting to know that these works have been translated into twenty-one languages.

--- SAYFA 256 ---

It was pleasing to learn that precautions have been taken to prevent the spread of malaria in these areas.

It is essential to ascertain that the roots are in close contact with the soil.

It is essential to ascertain that there is an adequate supply of raw materials near the factory site.

It is impossible to prove that the crime was committed at the time when this man was staying in a nearby town.

VII. NEDEN VE ETKİSİ STRÜKTÜRLERİ

a) Etkisi cümlenin fiilinden (veya bağlacından) sonra gelir.

b) Etkisi cümlenin fiilinden (veya bağlacından) önce gelir.

Cetvel

I ve II'ye bakınız. (Sayfa 260 ve 261)

Alıştırma

192. Cümlenin fiilini veya bağlacını bulup, birinci cetvele göre etkisiyle beraber tercüme ediniz. Sonra nedenini açıklayan parçaya bağlayıp bütün cümleyi Türkçeye çeviriniz:

--- SAYFA 257 ---

Lack of water is the most common cause of crop failure, and floods are also a very important cause of famine.

The ability to crush criticism is one of the causes of the success of dictators.

Earth movements during earthquakes are responsible for the folds in the rocks in the earth's crust.

In the virus infection poliomyelitis, damage to the cells of the motor nerves in the spinal cord causes the muscular paralysis of this disease.

Earth movements result in a series of enormous wrinkles in the crust of the earth.

Earth movements sometimes cause land to rise above the level of the surrounding ocean.

In the early history of the earth, violent earth movements caused blocks of the earth to be pushed many miles over other blocks.

Earthquakes have resulted in continents sinking below the sea.

Earthquakes have also caused large areas of the ocean bed to be raised to form the world's highest mountains.

The iron-nickel core at the centre of the earth produces the magnetic phenomena of the earth.

The irregular action of the sea may lead to swellings of the floor which give rise to shallow areas or islands.

There are also local conditions which result in variation in the form of the sea-floor and its deposits.

In these glacial fields the ice melted more rapidly in summer with the result that coarser material was deposited.

Deficiencies of the trace elements in the soil, such as manganese, boron, copper and zinc are responsible for many plant diseases.

The great mountain-building movements of the past have resulted in the intense folding of the rocks in many areas.

The introduction of goats on to the island has led to the devastation of the forests within a century.

There has been a great drought in this area and consequently plantation of trees has failed.

Sandy soil consists of large particles and as a result it is permeable to both air and water.

ezmek

tenkit, kritik

--- SAYFA 258 ---

Alıştırma

193. Cümlenin fiilini veya bağlacını bulup sayfa 261'deki ikinci cetvele göre etkisini ifade eden parçayı tercüme ediniz. Sonra nedenini açıklayan parçaya bağlayıp bütün cümleyi Türkçeye çeviriniz:

Their vitality and resistance to disease is low owing to the fact that their diet does not contain enough vitamins.

During the war between China and Japan, 15 per cent of the people in hospitals were suffering from disease owing to lack of Vitamin B.

The crops failed because of lack of water.

The muscular paralysis of poliomyelitis is caused by damage to the cells of the motor nerves in the spinal cord.

The success of dictators is partly due to their ability to crush criticism.

The folds in the rocks in the earth's crust result from earth movements during earthquakes.

Sandy soils are permeable to both air and water owing to the large size of their particles.

Many plant diseases are caused by deficiencies of trace elements such as manganese, boron, copper and zinc.

Devastation of the forests on the island resulted from the introduction of goats.

Plantation of trees in this area has failed owing to a severe drought.

Coarser material is deposited owing to the fact that the ice in these glacial lakes melts more rapidly in the summer.

Swellings on the floor of the ocean result from the irregular action of the sea.

Sözlük (Yukarıda verilen sözlüğe de bakınız)

İngilizce

Türkçe

vitality

canlılık

resistance

mukavemet, direnç

to suffer

hastalığa maruz kalmak, acı çekmek

Anlama Soruları

What caused the failure of the crops?

What causes the muscular paralysis of poliomyelitis?

What partly causes the success of dictators?

What causes the folds in the rocks in the earth's crust?

What causes sandy soils to be permeable to both air and water?

What causes many plant diseases?

What caused devastation of the forests on the island?

What caused the plantation of trees to fail in this area?

What causes coarser material to be deposited?

What causes swellings on the floor of the ocean?

SINIFLANDIRILMIŞ METİNLER

1. ADVERBIAL CLAUSES ONLY (ZARF CÜMLECİKLERİ)

SCIENCE

When a solid is heated, its molecules tend to move apart from each other so that it increases its volume. This increase becomes still more noticeable when the solid is fused. On the other hand, when a liquid body is solidified, its volume decreases because cooling brings the molecules closer together. However, water behaves differently. When it solidifies, its volume is increased by about one tenth. A closed bottle full of water, if its temperature falls below freezing point, will break, because in freezing, the water expands and exerts great pressure against the sides of the bottle. Water is less dense in the solid state than it is as a liquid, so that ice, if put into water, will float with part of its volume above the surface.

Kelimeler

noticeable: göze çarpan

fused: ergimiş

to float: yüzmek

Anlama Soruları

What is the result of this?

When does this increase become still more noticeable?

What happens when a liquid body is solidified?

Why does this happen?

What behaves differently?

What happens when water solidifies?

On what condition will a closed bottle full of water break?

Why will it break?

In which state is water less dense, in liquid or solid state?

How will ice float if put into water?

2. BOTANY, FORESTRY

If the seeds of a tree simply fell to the ground and germinated there, the young plants would be too crowded to survive. Also, if some disaster destroyed the parent tree, all its offspring would also be destroyed. Obviously it is better if the seeds can be carried away from the parent tree and be scattered over a wide area. Some seeds are dispersed by the plant itself. The fruit dries and contracts until it is under tension, like a spring, and the seeds are shot out when the fruit explodes. The squirting cucumber, a plant of the Mediterranean regions has a fruit like a small cucumber. When these are ripe, they burst away from the stalk and the seeds are thrown out as they do so.

--- SAYFA 263 ---

Other types of seed are dispersed by wind or by water, and some may be carried by animals or birds.

Kelimeler

to germinate: çimlenmek

to disperse: yaymak, dağıtmak

disaster: felaket

squirting cucumber: ebucehil kavunu, acıdülek, acıdürek

Anlama Soruları

What is obviously better?

What does the fruit do?

3. SCIENCE, BOTANY, FORESTRY

Although the greater part of the atmosphere consists of nitrogen, the nitrogen needed by plants and animals to build up their tissues is never available in sufficient quantities. This is due to the fact that pure nitrogen cannot be used for this purpose. It can be assimilated only when it is combined with other chemical elements, but our bodies have no power to make it combine in this way. If there were no bacteria in the soil, the world's supply of combined nitrogen would soon be finished. One very important genus of bacteria fixes free atmospheric nitrogen and combines it with other elements to make their own protoplasm. When the bacteria die, these nitrogenous compounds remain in the soil and are available for the nutrition of plants.

Anlama Soruları

What does a greater part of the atmosphere consist of?

Which nitrogen is never available in sufficient quantities?

When can it be assimilated?

What have our bodies no power to do?

What would happen if there were no bacteria in the soil?

What does one very important genus of bacteria do?

What happens when the bacteria die?

4. ECONOMICS

The requirements of the consumers are much less simple today than they were in former times. A merchant today has to try to provide goods as cheaply as he can without lowering the quality of the goods. He also has to create new types of goods when he sees a demand for them. This

--- SAYFA 264 ---

requires continual research into manufacturing and marketing processes, since the demand for goods often depends on fashion as much as it does on actual need. The quantity and variety of marketable goods is very great but we can form a clearer idea of them if we divide them into various classes.

5. MEDICINE

The heart is a hollow muscle. When it expands, blood pours into its cavities. When it contracts, the same blood is driven out into the arteries. If the body is engaged in work, the heart beats at an increased rate. The body automatically speeds up combustion when it works, in order that more energy is produced. Because more oxygen is required, and more carbon dioxide is produced, the heart must accelerate the circulation of the blood. On the wall of the right atrium of the heart, there are certain nerve discs sensitive to molecules of carbon dioxide. If a working muscle of the body produces carbon dioxide, molecules of this substance are rapidly carried to the heart, and acceleration begins. As soon as the muscle decreases its work, the rate of heart beat is correspondingly reduced.

Kelimeler

hollow: kovuk, boşluklu

to accelerate: hızlandırmak

circulation: dolaşım

to speed up: hızlanmak, hızlandırmak

correspondingly: ona göre, buna paralel olarak

Anlama Soruları

What is the heart?

What happens when it expands?

What happens when it contracts?

What happens if the body is engaged in work?

What does the body do when it works?

Why does it do this?

Why must the heart accelerate the circulation of the blood?

--- SAYFA 265 ---

To what are they sensitive?

6. LAW

In most trials the Crown acts as the prosecutor of the accused person but it is possible for individuals to bring a prosecution if an offence has been committed against themselves. If the case against the accused is proved, the Crown will sentence the accused in exactly the same way as if the Crown had prosecuted. In all criminal cases the accused is presumed innocent until he is proved guilty. No-one can be guilty of a crime by mistake. If a man is accused of poisoning his wife when he brought the wrong drug by mistake, he will not be found guilty of murder. If he was suffering from a defect of reason so that he was not responsible for his actions, he will be found 'Guilty but Insane'. In recent years this principle has been modified because Parliament has passed several Statutes to change the situation. Thus, if a shopkeeper gives short weight, he is guilty of an offence under the Weights and Measures Act, even if he didn't know. If a driver kills a pedestrian he may be found guilty of manslaughter even if he showed no intention to kill.

Kelimeler

the accused: sanık

by mistake: kazaen, yanlışlıkla

Crown: Kraliyet

pedestrian: yaya

defect: bozukluk, kusur

prosecution: savcılık, kovuşturma

drug: ilaç

to be found: sayılmak, bulunmak

insane: deli, akıl sağlığı bozuk

manslaughter: adam öldürme (kasıtsız)

prosecutor: savcı

reason: akıl

to sentence: hüküm giydirmek, cezalandırmak

short weight: eksik tartma

Anlama Soruları

7. PHILOSOPHY, HISTORY

The civilisation of Mycenae and of the Achaeans was destroyed in the eleventh century B.C. by the invasion of the Dorians. They did not conquer the whole of Greece but it was many centuries before the Greek peoples flourished as they had done in the Mycenaean age. The only centres of culture were to be found in the eastern Mediterranean. When they emerged in history again, in the seventh and sixth centuries B.C., the Dorians, Achaeans and other Greek people had settled down together as one people. They lived in independent city states and were often at war with one another. If they were threatened by attack from outside, they turned to Sparta for help, as they had done to Mycenae in earlier days.

Kelimeler

emerge: baş göstermek, çıkmak, belirmek

flourish: gelişmek, ilerlemek

invasion: akın, istila

people: millet, insanlar

settle down: yerleşmek

be threatened: tehdide uğramak, tehdit edilmek

8. HISTORY, ANTHROPOLOGY, LAW, SOCIOLOGY

If a man committed a crime, the burden fell on his whole family. They could defend him, but they could be the subject of the victim's revenge, as much as the criminal himself was. The injured family claimed from the criminal's family a fixed sum of money or goods to compensate for the injury. As time passed, however, other groups began to assume legal responsibility for justice. Now the law was not simply a matter of compensation. Although courts and punishments existed, the law was unwritten. Law courts did not become universal sources of justice until several hundreds of years had passed.

Kelimeler

burden: yük

matter: mesele, husus

revenge: intikam

responsibility: mesuliyet, sorumluluk

to assume: üzerine almak, üstlenmek

9. SCIENCE, ASTRONOMY

When a star begins its life, it is a vast, formless cloud of hydrogen gas and dust. This cloud begins to contract and rotate. As it contracts, the temperature at its centre increases and gradually, a burning young star is formed. When the temperature at its centre reaches $10\text{--}20 \text{ million } {}^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ the hydrogen gradually changes to helium through nuclear reactions. After hundreds of millions of years have passed, most of the hydrogen has changed to helium, and when this happens, the star increases in brightness and in size. Its radius may increase 300 times. If it becomes redder, it is known as a red giant. At this point, the star may explode and send its outer layers flying off into space. If this occurs, it is known as a nova. When it cools down it is called a white dwarf. The lifetime of a star varies from one to ten million years. So our sun will last another 5,000 million years before it starts to expand and explodes.

Kelimeler

brightness: parlaklık

dwarf: cüce

giant: dev

to explode: patlamak

Anlama Soruları

What does this cloud begin to do?

What is gradually formed?

When the temperature reaches $10\text{--}20 \text{ million } {}^{\circ}\mathrm{C}$ what happens?

When has most of the hydrogen changed to helium?

When this happens, what does the star do?

By how much may its radius increase?

When is it known as a red giant?

What may it do at this point?

What is it known as then?

What varies from one to ten million years?

10. SCIENCE, MATHEMATICS

Until recently, it has not been possible to measure the ground speed

--- SAYFA 268 ---

of an aircraft directly by instruments. But if the wind velocity is known, if the navigator wants to keep to a certain track, and if he knows both his airspeed and the wind velocity, he can use the triangle of velocities to discover the necessary course to follow. A course set by this method will be correct only as long as the wind velocity remains the same, and as long as its direction remains constant. In order that the aircraft should not be blown off course when the wind changes, the navigator must fix his position frequently so that he can check his calculations.

triangle: üçgen

to fix: tespit etmek

11. ECONOMICS

ADJECTIVAL CLAUSES ONLY (SADECE SIFAT CÜMLECİKLERİ)

An important development in the history of money was the introduction of bank-notes, which were pieces of paper that were issued by a bank. Anyone who presented the bank with the notes which it had issued could claim a fixed amount of gold or silver from the bank. Gradually, notes which were issued by a bank which was trustworthy, became generally accepted as a means of payment. From bank-notes, it was only a short step to cheques, which in Britain today are used for more than 90 per cent of transactions. A bank usually retains only 10 per cent of all its deposits on which cheques can be cashed, and by lending out or investing the remainder, a bank helps to create money. Anything which is freely accepted in payment of debts can be called money. In the Western world today, however, it almost always takes the form of currency or bank deposits which are accepted all over the world.

Kelimeler

to issue: çıkarmak, basmak (para vb.)

transactions: ticaret, iş, işlemler

to invest: para yatırmak, yatırım yapmak

trustworthy: güvenilir

deposit: yatırım, mevduat

to lend out: ödünç vermek, kredi vermek

--- SAYFA 269 ---

12. ECONOMICS

A factory is a building or group of buildings where a product is manufactured. In planning a factory, there are several things which must be taken into consideration. It should be in a place which can be reached easily by both the goods and the workers. It must be arranged to ensure a flow of materials from one section to another. Time which is spent in moving materials or men more than necessary is wasted. The buildings must be well-lit, well-heated and well-ventilated. All possible measures must be taken which will ensure the avoidance of accidents.

13. PHILOSOPHY, PSYCHOLOGY

The problem of the nature of human abilities which today carries much importance has been the subject of a great amount of research. It began in 1904 with Professor Spearman who was the most conspicuous figure in it. In his work in which he has developed his own theory and in which he has criticized the theories of others, he explains his two factors theory which, according to him, is based on the correlations between abilities.

14. FORESTRY, BOTANY, SCIENCE

The causes of disease and death in plants can be divided into three main categories: The first, which is the most common and dangerous, is the activity of other living organisms. These include grazing animals, insects, fungi, bacteria and viruses which are so small that they can be seen only with the electron-microscope. Viruses are the smallest of all living organisms and live only as parasites in the cells of plants or animals. In some ways they are intermediate between living and non-living organisms. Some form crystals when purified or concentrated. The potato suffers severely from virus disease, and many plants are infected by aphids whose winged forms carry the virus from one area to another. The second is unfavourable environment, such as excessive heat or cold, insufficient or excessive water, unsuitable soil. A plant can survive only in an environment to which it has adapted itself. The third is poisonous substances, especially smoke, fumes and effluents which are discharged into rivers from factories. The toxic substances which are produced by industrial processes destroy many plants every year. This is a problem of which society today is becoming increasingly aware, and which is generally known as pollution.

Kelimeler

grazing: otlayan

excessive: fazla, aşırı

intermediate: aralık cisim, ara, geçiş

environment: muhit, çevre

winged: kanatlı

effluents: dışarıya akan maddeler, atıklar

Anlama Soruları

15. MEDICINE, SCIENCE, FORESTRY, BOTANY, BIOLOGY

Bacteria have a structure which is similar to that of other living cells. They consist of protoplasm, which is the basic substance of living organisms, and which is composed of more than forty chemical elements. In the protoplasm there is a central structure which is similar to the nucleus of a cell. Surrounding the protoplasm there is a thin protective membrane which consists mainly of cellulose. Bacteria generally reproduce by splitting into two which is a method of reproduction that is known as fission or cell division. The nucleus divides first, the cell lengthens and grows thinner in the middle and finally the two parts separate. Some bacteria reproduce by sporation which is the production of a daughter-cell inside the protoplasm. This escapes by breaking through the cell-wall. Bacteria do not possess chlorophyll which is required to form their food material. For this reason they live as parasites of living organisms or as saprophytes on dead organic matter. Pathogenic bacteria are harmful to man, but the many others which are necessary to life are known as symbiotic bacteria.

Kelimeler

similar: benzer

to reproduce: üremek, çoğalmak

protective: koruyucu

to escape: çıkmak, kaçmak

Anlama Soruları

What is it composed of?

What does it consist of?

How does the daughter-cell escape?

16. SCIENCE, FORESTRY, BOTANY, BIOLOGY

The cell-wall is a membrane which encloses the cell, but which is not a living part of it. It is secreted by the cytoplasm and consists mainly of fibres of cellulose which are woven together. Sometimes it also contains carbohydrates such as pectin and lignin. This non-living cell-wall is a feature of plants which animal cells do not possess. The function of the cell-wall is to act as a protection and support for the cytoplasm. This is especially true of those parts of the plant which serve as supports, such as stems or branches. Here the cell walls which are rigid like little boxes, are impregnated with lignin. Wood is a mass of lignified cells. The cytoplasm is divided into two parts. The outer part, which is next to the cell-wall is the ectoplasm. This is a semi-permeable membrane which allows water which contains dissolved minerals to pass through. The inner part which is in continual motion is the endoplasm. The movement inside the cell is due to the continual chemical changes which take place in the cytoplasm. The plastids are small bodies which are suspended in the cytoplasm. There are three types of plastids. The chloroplasts which are the green corpuscles which contain chlorophyll. They use the energy in sunlight to combine carbon dioxide and water to produce sugars and oxygen. This is a process which is known as photo-synthesis. The leucoplasts are white round bodies whose function is to change into starch the sugars which are produced by the chlorophyll. The chromoplasts are yellow or orange bodies which have their origin in either the leucoplasts or the chloroplasts. The colour changes of leaves which take place in autumn are caused by these.

Kelimeler

to secrete: ifraz etmek, salgılamak

woven: dokunmuş

rigid: sert, bükülmeyen

body: cisim, gövde

impregnated: emprenye, içirilmiş

feature: özellik

Anlama Soruları

What does it also sometimes contain?

What is a feature of plants?

17. GEOGRAPHY, FORESTRY

The total amount of rain which falls during the year is an important climatic element, because of the control which this exerts over plant growth and therefore over the life of animals and man. At one extreme there are desert climates where rain is rare and few plants grow. In contrast to these, there are places which are near the equator where rainfall is plentiful throughout the year, and where plant growth is luxuriant. There is also the effect of seasonal rainfall which is important. Rain which falls in summer reduces the temperature and ensures moisture which assists plant growth. In some regions the winter is the wettest season, when rain falls outside the growing season. The system of climatic classification which was proposed by Köppen is very useful. It is a system which is based partly on average temperatures and rainfalls, and partly on temperature range. However, the system contains climatic boundaries which are difficult to recognise in nature. The line which divides two different types of climate does not correspond to any geographical distinctions which can be made according to vegetation, agriculture or population.

Kelimeler

desert: çöl

to be based: istinat etmek, dayanmak

to correspond: uymak, tekabül etmek

luxuriant: çok bol, gür

moisture: nem

boundary: hudut, sınır

distinction: fark, ayrım

climatic: iklimsel, iklime ait

Anlama Soruları

What is an important climatic element?

18. MEDICINE

Ulcers in the digestive system are known as peptic ulcers, but in order to distinguish those which occur in the stomach from those which occur in the duodenum, the names gastric ulcer and duodenal ulcer are often used. Peptic ulceration is a disease which has increased during the last 50 years, and it may be a disorder which is caused by the worry and tension of life in the twentieth century. The exact form of the injury which causes the mucosa of the alimentary tract to ulcerate remains unknown, but it may be the strong hydrochloric acid which is a gastric secretion. But this cannot be accepted as the only cause of injury.

Kelimeler

tension: gerginlik

secretion: ifrazat, salgı

to distinguish: ayırt etmek

worry: üzüntü, kaygı

disorder: rahatsızlık, bozukluk

19. LAW, ECONOMICS

The Welfare State is a national community which is organised to prevent any member from living at a level which is below a certain standard. In order to achieve this, its members contribute a certain amount of money into a central fund. In the nineteenth century people had to pay for many services which are now given free. Between 1906 and 1914

--- SAYFA 275 ---

the government introduced old age pensions, which guaranteed a regular income for old people; unemployment insurance and health insurance, regular contributions which would ensure an income during periods when a worker was unemployed or ill. These services were given to people who needed them, as a right, not as privileges.

Kelimeler

to contribute: vermek, ödemek, katkıda bulunmak

contribution: ücret, katkı, aidat

insurance: sigorta

privilege: imtiyaz, ayrıcalık

right: hak

welfare: sosyal refah

20. LAW, HISTORY

Peace and order were not natural conditions of life in the Middle Ages. A country which was without a strong and active ruler was a country in chaos. Henry I had the qualities which were necessary to bring his people the peace which they wanted. He was a man who understood the importance of money. The punishment for crime which was most often given was not death or imprisonment but a fine. Anyone who had a right to hold a court, had the right to keep the fines which were collected by it. A court which was well-run was therefore a source of great profit, and Henry ran his courts very well. These fines however, were not his chief source of money. He also raised taxes, but the chief difficulty was to collect them. Henry could not always trust his tax-collectors, so he developed a special department whose function was to collect taxes and to try men who had committed offences against the tax laws. These measures helped to bring peace and order which the country so much needed.

Kelimeler

tax: vergi

order: düzen

to run: idare etmek, yönetmek

a fine: para cezası

to try: yargılamak

chaos: düzensizlik, kaos

Anlama Soruları

What was a country in chaos?

Which qualities had Henry?

21. FORESTRY, BOTANY

A leaf is a complicated structure of cells and tissues which are enclosed between an upper and a lower skin. In the skin there are many tiny pores (or stomata) which open and close to regulate the rate at which gases enter and leave the leaf, and which control the loss of water-vapour. The stem which connects the leaf to the plant, and which carries water and nutrients to and from the plant, contains strong fibres which prevent the leaf from being torn away by the wind. The lamina whose microscopic internal structure includes the mesophyll, is usually thick in evergreen plants, whose leaves must resist the cold of winter. The palisade layer includes cells which are rich in chlorophyll which assists in photo-synthesis.

Kelimeler

to be enclosed: arasında bulunmak, çevrelenmek

to regulate: ayarlamak, düzenlemek

to include: dahil etmek, içermek

pores: gözenek

to connect: bağlamak

nutrients: besin, besin maddeleri

22. SCIENCE, MATHEMATICS

Computers use electrical currents and voltage to represent numbers. It is possible to design electrical circuits which have 10 different states to represent the 10 numerals of the decimal code, but it is easier to design them with only two states: One which represents the number 0 and another which represents 1. All numbers which are fed into the computer must be converted into the binary system of mathematics in which only the digits 1 and 0 are used.

The computer is given information in two parts – programme and data.

The programme contains instructions which tell the computer the tasks which it must perform (e.g. add, multiply, or print the answer).

The data are the numbers on which these mathematical operations must be carried out.

Information which is stored in the magnetic cones can be used at the speed of electric current, but they are not large enough to store all the information that is needed. Most computers also store information on magnetic tape which is less efficient than magnetic cone memory.

23. LITERATURE, PHILOSOPHY

Shelley was a poet who was in search of perfection, and his reputation is based on the poems which he wrote between 1818 and 1822. One of his best works which is considered his masterpiece is 'Prometheus Unbound', a long poem in which Shelley recreates and transforms the myth of Prometheus to embody his own

--- SAYFA 278 ---

philosophy and the view which that philosophy gave him of the world. Perhaps the poems for which he is now best remembered are the short lyrics, such as his 'Ode to the West Wind', 'To a Skylark', which express in language of unrivalled musical harmony and beauty his unique perception of nature.

The lines from 'The Cloud', which are given below, provide a suitable memorial to this great man who died so early, but who has become immortal through his poetry:

'I am the daughter of Earth and Water,

And nursling of the Sky.

I pass through the pores of the ocean and shores,

I change, but I cannot die.'

24. MEDICINE

When a knife cuts the skin, the blood begins to escape from the broken blood vessels. After it has filled the space in the wound, it begins to run out on to the surface of the skin. When the blood reaches the air, it begins to form a clot, and bleeding ceases. Within 24 hours, the blood vessels on each side of the wound begin to develop tiny branches which rapidly grow and enter the clot which fills the wound. Millions of long thin cells which are known as fibroblasts appear, whose function is to bind the two sides of the wound together. The cut edges of the skin grow across the top of the wound until they meet in the middle and form a scab. When this falls off, the scar tissue can be seen as a purple line, which gradually turns white. This is the scar which in some cases marks

--- SAYFA 279 ---

the site of the wound for life, and which does not have the elasticity of the skin.

25. MEDICINE, SCIENCE

Tetanus is caused by a spore-bearing bacterium which occurs in soil, manure and dust. It usually finds its way into human tissues when one of these materials penetrates a cut or injury. When it has penetrated the tissues, the microbe produces its characteristic toxin which travels up the nerve fibres and so reaches the spinal cord and brain. The effect of this toxin on the nerve cells of the central nervous system is to make them discharge streams of nerve impulses which cause painful muscular contractions. Because the jaw muscles are almost always affected, the disease is sometimes called lockjaw, but muscles in all parts of the body may be affected.

Penicillin is given to kill the tetanus microbes in the tissues. Anti-tetanic serum is given to neutralise the toxin, which is formed by the bacteria, and muscle relaxing drugs are given to reduce the spasms of the muscles. Tetanus can be prevented by vaccination and most children are vaccinated against this disease when they have their diphtheria and whooping cough inoculations. People who are not immunised in this way are usually protected by a dose of anti-tetanic serum when their injury is treated in hospital.

26. FORESTRY, BOTANY

Biennial plants are herbaceous plants which produce leaves during their first season of growth, and flower during the second season, after which they die. Plants which continue to live and flower for a number of seasons are called perennials. Most of them are trees and shrubs which have woody stems, but there are herbaceous perennials which survive because they store food underground. An underground stem which is swollen with stored food lives through the winter and enables the plant to resume growth in the spring. Such stems are known as rhizomes.

Lichens are the greenish-grey or yellow, moss-like plants which grow on trees or rocks, and they are amongst the longest lived of all plants. After they have grown rapidly for about 10 years, they then grow very slowly for an indefinite period. The life of lichen which grows on trees is limited by the life of the tree, but lichen which grows on rock may live for hundreds or even thousands of years.

27. FORESTRY, BOTANY

Although beech trees (Fagus sylvatica) are found in many places in Britain, they form extensive woodlands only on chalk or on limestone formations. The woods are never completely felled, but a certain number of trees of different sizes are taken out at intervals, and the loss is replaced by the natural growth and self-sowing of the trees which remain. The bark remains smooth however old the tree, and the tree reaches a height of about 100 feet in as many years. It continues to increase its diameter for a long time after this. The leaves are smooth and covered with a silvery-white down, which protects them from early frosts.

In stands where beech is predominant, shade is so dense that few smaller trees or plants can grow. Yew and holly are sometimes found because, since they are evergreens, they can grow in early spring when the branches of the beech are bare. In very dense beech stands, almost the only ground-living plants are those which live on decaying vegetable material, that is, saprophytes.

28. GEOGRAPHY, GEOLOGY

When we speak of volcanic activity, we include all the phenomena which are associated with the escape at the earth's surface of magmatic materials from the depths. A violent eruption of hot lava, dust and gases is usually only the end of a phase of activity which may involve nearly continuous eruptions, explosions and earth tremors. A volcano which has erupted in recent times is called active.

A volcanic eruption may take many forms. If the magma is stiff and sticky, the gases may burst out in an explosion. The lava is shot upwards as rocks, ashes and cinders which rain from the sky for some time afterwards. If the magma is a free-flowing liquid, the gases which it contains may only bubble to the surface with few violent explosions. When the lava rises, it may overflow the crater or break through fissures in its sides. About 500 volcanoes are known to be active, most of which are found along the lines of recent mountain-building belts.

29. GEOGRAPHY

Although there are differences in the level between the Great Lakes, a system of locks and canals has made navigation possible between them. The Lakes play an important part in the iron and steel industry which exists all over that area. The raw materials have to be transported long distances from where they are mined to where they can be made into steel and used for industrial purposes. At the western end of the Lakes there are vast iron-ore deposits so that many mines have been established there. At the eastern end, coal deposits are found which are suitable for the manufacture of steel. It is between these two points that the great cargo ships travel. Iron ore which is found at the western end of Lake Superior is transported by ship at a rate of 50 million tons per year. Grain which is grown on the western prairies is transported before the lakes freeze over at the end of the year.

30. ECONOMICS

The price of goods depends to some extent on the law of supply and demand. If goods are available in large quantities, they will tend to be cheap. But if a large number of people want to purchase goods which are scarce, the price will rise. The price of goods also depends on the actual cost of production. This is the total cost of all the expenses which are incurred in making the goods. First there is the cost of the raw materials, which includes the

--- SAYFA 284 ---

cost of labour, machinery, fuel and transport from the source to the factory. When the raw materials are processed in the factory, further expenses are incurred. These include the wages of workmen and office staff, and the cost of operating and maintaining the machinery which is used. But capital has also been invested in the factory, the purchase of land, the building and purchase of machinery. The interest which is paid on this capital must also be added to the cost of the goods. Then there are also the costs of packing and transport of the goods, insurance, taxes and customs duties which must also be added to the cost of production.

Goods may be sent direct for sale in shops or markets, or they may first go to the wholesaler, who buys them from the factory, before he distributes them to the retailer. Both the wholesaler and the retailer have to pay the costs of their warehouses and shops, and these, together with the costs of transport, packing and advertising, make up the cost of distribution. When all these are added together the retail selling price can be found.

31. LAW

There are some countries which possess forms of government which can be classed as liberal democracy. None of these countries is a direct democracy as Athens was, because they are too large and complex. They are representative democracies, in which the voting is not so much for persons as for the political parties to which they belong. Although the political parties are important to the working of the system of government, they are not essential to the idea of democracy. The system would not be less democratic if all the candidates were independent. In Great Britain, the candidate who gets the most votes is elected, and the party which has the most elected candidates is in power. In other countries, various systems of proportional representation are used, by which some seats in parliament are distributed according to the national totals of votes to certain parties. Some countries have a preferential vote in which electors make a list of candidates in order of preference, instead of choosing only one.

32. SOCIOLOGY, ANTHROPOLOGY, HISTORY

The first men were hunters and gatherers. Their food consisted of the animals which they could catch and kill, and the edible fruits, leaves and roots which they could find around them. They spent almost all their lives in search of food. When they had exhausted the resources of the area in which they lived, they moved to another area. Hundreds of thousands

--- SAYFA 286 ---

of years later, men learnt to herd instead of hunt, and to cultivate rather than to forage. The first farmers probably lived about 6,000 B.C. in the warm lands at the eastern end of the Mediterranean. In those days, the climate of that area was wetter than it is today, and therefore it was ideal for agriculture. Their herds were a reliable source of meat and also provided milk and carried loads.

Men also learned to save some of the edible seeds which they had collected each summer, for planting the following spring in ground which they had prepared. When the crops ripened, they ate only part of the grain; they saved the remainder and again planted it as seed the following year. These advances had important effects. They released men from their endless search for food and made it possible for them to live in permanent settlements. Later when a man was able to grow more food than his family needed, he could barter some of the extra for other goods which a neighbour could supply. In this way the techniques of civilisation arose.

NOUN CLAUSES ONLY (SADECE İSİM CÜMLECİKLERİ)

33. MEDICINE, SCIENCE

Until 300 years ago, almost everyone believed that epidemics were caused by evil spirits. Even doctors thought that the terrible disease of cholera was caused by an evil spirit of some kind. Bacteria are invisible to the naked eye, so they could not know that they existed. In the middle of the eighteenth century, Needham claimed to have proved that bacteria were generated by supernatural means. Spallanzani proved that Needham's ideas were mistaken. He knew that microscopic creatures die in boiling water, so he put seeds in water in two glass bottles. He sealed one and left the other with a loose-fitting cork. Then he put the two bottles into boiling water for an hour and left them to stand for several days. He found that the sealed bottle contained no bacteria and that the other one was full of them. From this he deduced that bacteria had been carried by the air. Pasteur later showed that the fermentation of wine and beer is caused by micro-organisms in the air. In 1928 Fleming noticed that a culture of bacteria was killed by the growth of a mould or fungus.

34. HISTORY, GEOGRAPHY

The defeat of the Armada demonstrated to all the world that the rule

--- SAYFA 288 ---

of the seas had passed from the Mediterranean peoples to the Northern peoples. This meant that the Reformation would survive in Northern Europe and that the Northerners would lead the world in the new oceanic era. Drake maintained that there should be a complete understanding between the Royal Navy and the merchant adventurers. The technical differences between the tactics of a Spanish and an English ship showed clearly that there was a great difference in social character between Spain and England. Drake knew that discipline was needed on his ships but not feudalism. The ideas and manners of Spain, however, were still feudal.

35. MEDICINE

Acute otitis media in children is a common disease in general practice. In 1961 Dr. Fry found that 10 per cent of the children in his practice had one or more attacks per year. In 1957 the Medical Research Council reported that the yearly incidence was 8 per cent. It is known that deafness is present during an attack, but there seems to be little evidence that these effects are long-term.

37. LAW, ECONOMICS

In the nineteenth century the doctrine was widely held that the State should not interfere with individuals. Many attempts to improve bad conditions by legislation were opposed with the belief that the government should not interfere with the principle of 'laissez-faire'. In spite of the opposition, however, legislation was introduced and it established the principle that the State had a duty to ensure that the members of the community had a certain basic standard of living.

38. GEOGRAPHY, GEOLOGY, FORESTRY

Some geologists believe that the earth is heating up. We can assume that a particle of uranium in a piece of granite was originally pure uranium. We find that the particle contains a certain amount of lead, and

--- SAYFA 290 ---

so we know that it has been decaying for a very long time. The rate of decay is constant, so an analysis of the relative amounts of lead and uranium in the particle will tell us how long it has been decaying; that is, how long ago the rock was formed.

39. BOTANY, BIOLOGY, ZOOLOGY, HISTORY

Until the late 18th century, it was believed that various kinds of mythical animals existed. The world was inadequately explored at that time, and it was thought that they might exist somewhere. Early naturalists did not realise that living organisms can come into existence only as the offspring of parents of their own kind. They knew that this was true among higher animals, but they thought that maggots, for example, were produced by 'spontaneous generation' in rotting matter. The ancient Egyptians thought that the scarab beetle was born out of the mud of the Nile. Until the 16th century it was believed that a kind of wild goose was generated from shell-fish.

Aristotle was the first to propose that animals should be classified systematically. He divided them into two groups according to whether they possessed red blood or not. He understood enough to know that whales and dolphins were not fish, but he believed that a swarm of bees generated from the dead body of an ox. The truth is that flies resembling bees lay their eggs in the dead body, and flies of the same kind emerge. Final proof that all life comes from existing life was the work of Louis Pasteur.

Kelimeler

İngilizce

Türkçe

mythical

inadequately

kabuklu böcek

balina balığı

oğul, sürü (arı vb.)

maggot

40. SCIENCE, BOTANY, BIOLOGY, FORESTRY

In the early years of this century, botanists found that certain plants had their roots covered with tiny tubercles. They assumed that the plants were suffering from a kind of disease. But later they discovered that the soil, after the death of the plants, became more fertile than before. They realised that this was due to an increase in the amount of combined nitrogen in the soil. The tubercles were examined under the microscope and it was found that they were full of bacteria. It was soon established that these have the power of fixing atmospheric nitrogen. It is true to say that life on earth could not exist without the action of these bacteria.

Kelimeler

tubercle: yumrucuk

to establish: tespit etmek, kanıtlamak

What was soon established?

What is it true to say?

41. PHILOSOPHY, SCIENCE

In the explanation of the scientific discovery, there was a great difference between what had actually happened and what had been published. The lecturer told how the report had been written and said that he would now explain how the experiments had been carried out. What he said was more interesting and was more easily understood than what the published report contained. He was asked why he had not published the full account, and he explained that he could not report more for publication than what could be checked by repeatable experiments. He

--- SAYFA 292 ---

added that what could not be verified by repeatable experiments could not be included in his report.

42. PHILOSOPHY, SCIENCE

To understand a scientific idea it is not enough merely to obtain a statement of it. One must see its point, and see what intellectual demands it satisfies. One must understand what problems are involved and what other attempts have been made in previous times and why they were unsatisfactory. The author of a scientific idea must explain how he perceived the problem and what obstacles he had to overcome.

43. FORESTRY, BOTANY, BIOLOGY

It has been mentioned that insufficient light delays flowering, but it must be remembered that the mycelia of many fungi grow well in darkness. However, we know that light is essential for the reproduction of functional sporophores, and we have observed that mosses growing in poorly lighted caves usually remain vegetative. It has been seen that the herbaceous plants growing under forest canopies show great differences in the period of maximum flowering, depending on whether the trees are

--- SAYFA 293 ---

evergreen or winter-deciduous. Tree leaves in the deciduous type of forest do not open until late spring.

44. BOTANY, BIOLOGY, PHILOSOPHY, FORESTRY

Early ecologic thought was dominated by anthropomorphism and teleology. Anthropomorphism is the habit of attributing human characteristics to non-human subjects. An example is the expression that a plant 'avoids' acid soils. Teleology is the doctrine that adaptation is purposive; for example, in the statement that the wing of a seed is 'made for' wider dissemination. It was assumed that such an adaptation was made in response to a particular need, and it may appear that such an assumption is correct. However, close analysis shows that not all responses of plants to environmental stimuli are beneficial. Experiments have shown that many responses, whether they are beneficial or not, can be explained on a physical or chemical basis.

Kelimeler

to attribute: atfetmek, yüklemek

adaptation: intibak, adaptasyon

beneficial: yararlı, faydalı

dissemination: dağılma, yayılma

response: cevap, tepki

Anlama Soruları

Give an example of anthropomorphism.

What is the doctrine of teleology?

Give an example of teleology?

What was assumed?

What may appear?

What does close analysis show?

What have experiments shown?

45. PSYCHOLOGY

In memorising, we have asked whether the job should be finished in one sitting or whether it is better to spread the learning over a number of periods. Experiments have been carried out to decide which method is best. For example, two similar groups of people were given material to memorise. The first group read the material 16 times in one day. The

--- SAYFA 294 ---

other group also read the material 16 times, but at the rate of one reading a day for 16 days. Each group was tested to see how much had been remembered. The results showed that there was a great difference between the two groups. The first group remembered 9 per cent and the second group remembered 79 per cent of the material, in spite of the fact that there was more opportunity to forget during the 16-day period of learning.

Kelimeler

to memorise: ezberlemek

in one sitting: bir oturumda

similar: benzer

in spite of: -e rağmen

opportunity: fırsat

period: müddet, süre, dönem

Anlama Soruları

What have we asked? (2 things)

Why have experiments been carried out?

Why was each group tested?

What did the result show?

In spite of what did they remember 79 per cent?

46. LAW, ECONOMICS

Governments throughout the world assume that the welfare of their people depends on the economic strength and wealth of the community. However, it is obvious that the strength of a country's economy depends also on the efficiency of its agriculture and industry; and that this depends upon the efforts of scientists and technologists. It also means that governments are compelled to interfere in these spheres, in order to increase production; they must also ensure that it is used in the best way. In order to do this, the governments must have advice from technical experts and scientists of all sorts. It follows that scientists are involved in government, and in politics, regardless of whether they like it.

Kelimeler

efficiency: verimli işleme, verimlilik

sphere: alan, küre, saha

to be compelled: mecbur olmak, zorunlu olmak

to depend on: bağlı olmak

to interfere: karışmak, müdahale etmek

advice: öğüt, tavsiye, danışmanlık

Anlama Soruları

What do governments assume?

What is obvious? (2 things)

What does this also mean?

What must they ensure?

What follows?

47. SCIENCE, PHILOSOPHY

It has been asked what the nature of the scientific attitude really is. We all know that science plays an important role in our societies and many people believe that our progress depends upon two different aspects of science. The first is technology. It is true that through technology, science improves the structure of society and that in this way it helps man to gain

--- SAYFA 295 ---

greater control over his environment. The second aspect is the application by all members of society of scientific methods of thought and action. But we must ask what these methods are. It seems that a successful scientist is full of curiosity; he wants to find out how and why the universe works. He thinks that he can improve the existing conditions. Also, a scientist is sceptical and does not believe that anything is true without careful and objective experiment.

Kelimeler

aspect: cephe, yön, bakış açısı

environment: muhit, çevre

application: tatbik, uygulama

curiosity: öğrenmek merakı, merak

sceptical: şüpheci

progress: ilerleme

What do we all know?

48. MEDICINE, SCIENCE

A chance observation often starts a new field of investigation. For example, Sir Alexander Fleming found that during his absence from his laboratory, a mould had grown on a culture medium containing pathogenic bacteria. He noticed that the bacteria near the mould had stopped growing. He concluded that the mould had the power to kill the bacteria, and this led to the discovery of penicillin.

Kelimeler

chance: tesadüf, rastlantı

to conclude: sonuca varmak

mould: küf

medium: ortam

Anlama Soruları

What did Sir Alexander Fleming find?

What did he notice?

What did he conclude?

What did this lead to?

49. GEOLOGY, GEOGRAPHY

Early peoples did not understand what caused earthquakes. The Greeks believed that the god of the sea was angry. Later Greek thinkers came to the conclusion that earthquakes were caused by storms in huge underground caves. Today we know that they are caused by the continual process of structural adjustment within the solid structure of the earth. They occur in 'young' mountain areas of the world. This means that these mountains have been formed only recently. Seismology is the study of earthquakes

--- SAYFA 296 ---

and the seismograph is an instrument used to measure them. It records the exact time and intensity of earth tremors.

Kelimeler

god: ilah, tanrı

to record: kayıt etmek

adjustment: ayarlama, uyum, düzeltme

tremor: titreme, sarsıntı

Anlama Soruları

What did early peoples not understand?

What did the Greeks believe?

To what conclusion did later Greek thinkers come?

What do we know today?

Where do earthquakes occur?

What does this mean?

What is seismology?

What is the seismograph?

What does it record?

50. GEOLOGY, HISTORY

Palaeontologists know that for some reason, reptiles largely became extinct at the end of the Mesozoic era. It is thought that widespread changes in climatic conditions were the cause of this. But it is not known how the mammals managed to survive. It must be remembered that they had warm blood and coats of hair to insulate their bodies from the changes in temperature. It has been discovered that reptiles must hibernate in winter, due to the fact that they cannot be active in the cold. It is true that there are hibernating mammals but this is due to the fact that their food is scarce during the winter season.

Kelimeler

extinct: soyu tükenmiş, yok olmuş

era: çağ, dönem

mammal: memeli hayvan

to insulate: izole etmek, yalıtmak

to hibernate: kış uykusuna çekilmek

scarce: kıt

Anlama Soruları

When did reptiles largely become extinct?

What is thought to be the cause of this?

What has been discovered?

51. SCIENCE, ASTRONOMY

Until a few years ago it was incorrectly thought that between earth and space was only a layer of atmosphere about 100 miles thick. We now

--- SAYFA 297 ---

know that the earth is surrounded by two radiation belts. Scientists have found that Venus has little or no magnetic field and therefore no radiation belt. Physicists believe that the earth's magnetism is caused by its rotation and the movement of its liquid interior. So it seems probable that Venus either rotates very slowly or not at all. Instruments have also been used to detect the heat and radio waves emitted by Venus. These showed that the surface beneath its dense cloud layer has a temperature of about $800^{\circ}\mathrm{F}$. So it seems probable that Venus cannot support any form of life known on earth.

Kelimeler

belt: kuşak

to detect: keşfetmek, algılamak, tespit etmek

interior: iç taraf, iç kısım

probable: muhtemel

Anlama Soruları

What was incorrectly thought until a few years ago?

What do we now know?

What have scientists found?

What do physicists believe?

What seems probable?

What have instruments been used to detect?

What did these show?

What seems probable?

52. HISTORY, HISTORY OF ART, ANTHROPOLOGY, PHILOSOPHY

The Greek writer Herodotus stated that the Egyptians were the most religious people of mankind. They worshipped many gods and believed that they were owners of the universe. They also believed that the gods were the source of Egypt's prosperity. Their gods appeared in paintings and sculptures, some with human and others with animal heads. Heliopolis, city of the sun, was the centre where the sun-god was worshipped as the highest. The sun-god Ra was lord of heaven and creation and he had many forms. His priests taught that Ra was the first King of Egypt and that all other kings were descended from him.

At first the early Egyptians believed that a dead body came to life again at certain times. Later the idea arose that the spirit (Ka) came back to life. They also believed that the dead were judged by the rulers of the land of the dead. It was also thought that punishment could be avoided by the use of certain magic charms.

Kelimeler

religious: dindar

prosperity: refah

spirit: ruh

charm: büyü, tılsım

god: tanrı

to worship: tapmak

priest: rahip

to be judged: yargılanmak

--- SAYFA 298 ---

53. HISTORY, ANTHROPOLOGY

It is thought that the first farmers belonged to the Neolithic age. It used to be thought that there was a gap between the primitive nomadic life of the Palaeolithic Age and the rural village economy of the Neolithic. However, it is now known that there was no such gap. It is now believed that a number of hunting-fishing cultures existed during the interval. It has been discovered that Neolithic communities with domestic animals and farming techniques existed in northern and western Europe.

Kelimeler

a gap: ara boşluk, boşluk, kopukluk

domestic: evcil

rural: kırsal

interval: ara, aralık

54. LAW, PHILOSOPHY, SOCIOLOGY

The Declaration of Human Rights is not a treaty. It is a statement of what nations agree should be their aim. A number of nations agreed that human beings ought to have their many rights listed in the Declaration. The United Nations declared in 1948 that the Declaration established a common standard of achievement for all nations.

--- SAYFA 299 ---

Article 19 claims that every individual has a right to education. So far, nations have not been able to agree that these rights should be expressed in one treaty. The United Nations decided that education should be dealt with by UNESCO – the United Nations Educational, Scientific and Cultural Organisation. The main purpose of this organisation is to ensure that all children shall have the same right to education whatever the race, religion or political opinions of their parents may be.

Kelimeler

declaration: beyanname, deklarasyon

achievement: başarı

race: ırk

right: hak

to be dealt with: idare edilmek, ele alınmak

opinion: kanaat, fikir, görüş

What is UNESCO?
